Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which the first way is that you make three cauteries or four, aligning according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cautery at once, and let the patient often turn on their back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the core which is located at the mouse, where the side of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevation from which you lift the core be according to the core, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.  
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After he puts in the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, then pull out the fire, and thus it will have four. And if you see, if it cauterizes with all the fire to three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has festered for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures before mentioned. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is of no value to a person with dropsy, except in the manner which is called "ascending".  
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the belly, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the thigh, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place the breast; and let the cauteries be very close to the hope of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery uncovered for a long time to prevent decay, and do not leave the patient's wound unattended after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be a pin as we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been mentioned before. 
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet 
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is hydrocephalic and are full of clear fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go in too deeply, so that the clear fluid will be driven out, and let the cautery be according to this form: 
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries exposed for a long time without cleaning, so that it dries out; then cure the other cures that we have said. 
de la menoison	From the menstruation  
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by ways of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with strong greenness, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the stomach cautery, or the circling cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle with each cautery a subtle pin, and two cauteries on the thighs. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the shoulder blade, and one cautery on each knee, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the navel, for the treatment is profitable when there is good help. 
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids  
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or more, and they are old and are of large, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, those that are all behind below the shoulder blade one by one in a triangular fashion, and one cautery below the buttocks two times; and if you think that his stomach is cooled and the meat does not cook, and one sees swelling in the face, then on the face make one large cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cautery open for a long time.  
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place until it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul" 
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut thethelul, if you heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then put it all ablaze upon that thelul cut; and let it stay as long as your hand and the cauteries reach the beginning of the vein, so that the blood stops; do this one or two times, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each one as we have said; afterward cure with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize a large cautery upon the flesh, it will be more helpful.  
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound 
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer cutting nor opening, which we will relate in its place, then comes a certain illness that cannot be healed except by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes to someone, and it is old and has foul putrefaction and corrupted moisture, if you must prove its depth at once with a subtle probe, and be sure that you know at once the entire depth of how far it goes. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After you heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and put it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and begin again with the cautery until those rotten and corrupted flesh are burned, once or two or three times, according to the quantity needed; and beware of burning the nerves which are there, and the large veins.  
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the flesh of the bladder and the intestines, then beware of those places, and do not make these efforts except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not a through-and-through wound; after healing the place until it is healthy, and if the place is salty, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is healed entirely; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is bad, and the bone at its base is corrupted; and thus as one of those that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	Of the sickness of the kidneys 
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and does not take pleasure from a woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with a pointed cautery as we have previously said; and if we cauterize them in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder 
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the back part above the bladder, where the pubic hairs begin, on the right and on the left; and let each cautery be as long as the knuckle of a finger; and make one cautery on the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be pointed according to the form previously mentioned. 
de la marris	From the sea 
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, there is great pain; then it is necessary to make III cauteries around the hip, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and II cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be sharp, as we have said. 
de la hainche	From the hip 
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moistures descend to the socket of the hip and for this reason it moves from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and if two sides are found in the division, then you must cauterize the patient on the socket of the hip with I cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is inside the circle; and let the cauteries be like those with which one has cauterized the stomach. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make three large olive-wood cauteries, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all hearts; and burn it until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip 
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip bone, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure is worthless, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterward, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, together burning medicines, and fire cautery.  
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, of which one is this: that you cauterize on the hip bone three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good depth and large, and let there be space between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive wood; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cautery is applied with a circle as we have previously said in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the whole hip, and all the muscles of the heart are burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is held, and one cautery on top of the ankle four times, on the left side a poke; and let the cauteries be lancets, and burn the thickness of the flesh; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, cauterize him where he feels the pain three points or four with the cautery which is called "points". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a knife-like or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more pain and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot and left it so long that the leg was all swollen, and the foot too, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After which a belly solution led to his death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. 
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, how this is the manner, make such an iron and let it at the head as thick as a nail of a doctor, or a bit less, and let it be between the notches and from one notch to the other a space the quantity of a knuckle; and let the notches be opposite two sides, and be also like knots, and there is a handle of iron well made; and this is the form. 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and gives off sparks, and then put it on the box of the sick hip, and let it be turned on the healthy side; and the cauterizer once the cautery has gone out and leaves it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the cure of anointing until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its appearance, and we rarely see anyone who uses it; and nevertheless it is a good cautery for those who can endure it and where it applies. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning medical cauteries are such that you make the instrument at intervals so that it descends along the edge of the door, and it is made of brass or iron with a long handle, and in height it has two notches, and between each one the thickness of a finger; and they are open on the outside and above, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Afterwards, place the box on the patient's hip while lying on his healthy side; then press your hand very firmly on top of the hip box; afterwards insert between the two circles of the hot awl which has been heated in the fire for a short time and leave it there for an hour or so, letting the patient endure the heat and burning. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it also finds biting like fire; and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip with a soft bandage, and leave it for three days, and put butter on it until what is black from the burn is removed; and leave it for three days so that decay can be extracted; and this would be the last help after the cure of ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, make the instrument that has a bandage according to what you have done in the hip similarly; and this is the manner of hot bandages, and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot coals, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole so that the point of a razor can enter; and put one pot over the other well sealed, and put alkali and hot and sweet water on it, as much as there is two fingers above the powders when you have well pressed it with your hand; and leave it like this until clear water and cheese or fat comes out, then take all that water and pour it on the hot and alkali just as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very watery and is administered in a soft form for medical treatments and cauteries of other members because it does the work like fire; and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes well, such as turpentine, and honey and anacardia and hot water with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a remedy by which a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic nerve, and praised it highly, saying that no other remedy was used, and that he was healed in a single time when this remedy was done, and he bathed as he teaches below. 
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in this manner that you take two drachms of fresh and dried green litharge, and grind it very fine with a bit of fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and tie it; and leave it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter a bath so that his body is warmed a little, and let him enter a bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hairs, it helps a lot; and the cautery must be done in this manner. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow which is between the thumb of the foot and the other one which is called the knuckle. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After take goat horns, and soak them in fire until they are charcoal, and put them on wool, and leave them until they are extinguished; and do so again, and do not cease to do so until you think by feeling that it reaches the hip, and that the pain is gone; and this manner of cautery is called "goat horn cautery." 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back  
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or percussion or excessive evacuation, or by similar spread of cold matter, none of these resemblances are worth cautery, except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter.  
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is fitting after that the patient has been emptied of fetid pills or other similar things, that one makes on the back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with an inch, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "points"; and if you see fit, make three cauteries or four at a moderate hot iron cautery according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight airway when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and on us the appearance that comes upon the other spines. 
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to heal it, cauterize it with a cautery of iron according to this form. 
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	Make sure the cautery touches each part of the spine equally. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery making two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterward heal the place until it is healthy according to what we have said, and be careful that you do not administer a cautery in a spasmodic area that is in a nerve’s grasp. 
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints 
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints is from humors that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the foot, which the wise call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-oil based according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you burn on the surface of the foot, make a cautery at every point that one calls "point". 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and to other joints, which happens many times, make a cautery on each knee three or four on each side, all olive-oil based; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand too long so that only the thickness of the heart is burned.  
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and the back, apply the cautery that we have described in our chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two points around the wristbone; and if there is still pain in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the elbows or as far as the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and administer medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sinew  
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the groin, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is new, it is fitting that when you have him cleaned, he should not eat anything that day; and he should use things which loosen the belly, so that his intestines descend from his belly; afterward make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath as long as the bowels are being repaired, and reset them at your will, and press down below the rupture on the bone of the wrist, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in this shape: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and it drips sap. 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and have the attendant hold his hand so that they do not return backwards; and work the thighs of the patient well, and put a cushion and a sergeant on the thighs, and another on the foot which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; and be careful that the eye does not protrude when you are making the cautery so that you do not burn it; and so that by this the patient does not die or suffer other ills. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their age, and those for adults be large according to their size; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; afterwards cure it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and it is fitting that his bandages be loosened for a long time so that the eyeball does not protrude when he prepares to go into chambers. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him be given a well-made bandage, and let him wear it for forty other days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against too much repletion of drinking and eating, and from excessive loud shouting; and when he follows these instructions he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here afterward the treatment of the waist in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	of a rupture of the belly 
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make the cautery according to its quantity, and burn one-third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place of the incision and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another behind, and hold your hand steady on all sides with the heated cautery. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of pain in any limb old 
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or a wound, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "points," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and turns and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for this custom is that it should move to the member closest to it, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed. 
de meselerie	of healing 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Healing is aided many times by cautery with great help, and even the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see it necessary to cauterize, take care if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will infect the whole patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one on the nape of the neck, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the back of the head; and leave your hand there until the cauteries reach the bone, and so that the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize according to what is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the measles is scattered all over; and it clearly loses its power, then you must cauterize it with those cauteries that we have mentioned above, or one cautery on the nape of the neck, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on each elbow, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are above the last bone of the heel, lest you burn them; and never cauterize a bone in the arm, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more help you give, and the better it works; and know that patients do not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already all corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, dust the area with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be a small prick entering the thickness of the flesh; then treat it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauteries are made on the hand and foot and back, at the point where the nerve that moves the limb emerges, and thus the swelling is removed; but let no one interfere with this unless they know the limbs and the emergence points of the nerves that move the body.  
de albaras	From aloes 
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness which is called “albaras” has aged, and medicines are of no avail, then cauterize with a cautery a spot perfect, according to the quantity of the species of the heart, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of beans and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of pigeon and blood of almond, of each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it at the place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a chancre by cautery 
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you see it stop, if you cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the chancre.  
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nevertheless the sages say that one should also apply a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and nevertheless it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen several times; and something further is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular," as we have said in the discussion of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move  
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a condition called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal, either due to the excess that it causes or because of the patient's weakness (that is to say, they are too old) and have little blood, or because of time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it thus. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through the whole cautery, heat the cautery as follows: 
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that sickness which is called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in half a way so that the course of the rot is alleviated. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed. 
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron 
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of sickness which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a consuming of the limbs, for it gnaws at the limbs just as fire devours dry reeds. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this sickness in a place that can suffer cautery along with fire, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to what suits the place where the sickness is; after cauterizing on all sides until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything which is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the wounds cauterized embers crushed with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of wounds engendering flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, start the cautery again on that which remains corrupted from the wounds. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this treatment has sometimes been cured with boiled water instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the treatment with boiled water in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of purples that come to the feet 
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that at the feet by fires a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large foul thing that bleeds the foot.  
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this illness are according to two manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot iron cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat a cautery tip as thin as a quill, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and that it has subtle edges; then you put it all heated on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it so for 3 days until it begins to rot; then you make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nails will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.  
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place of application by smearing lard until it is healed. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire on the body, and it often happens in the hands and feet, then you must apply a hot cautery to it; and it is done in this way: take a cane of iron or wood, or a goose quill, and put it on the wart and the callus, that is to say for warts.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you have extracted all those that are on the body, then cure the wounds which breed flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for trembling. 
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold of nerves, or a quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you make them four cauteries or IV on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; this will leave the trembling, and hasten the health from the cold illness. 
des pustules puans	Of stinking pustules. 
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear throughout the body, baths or stinking pustules, which come from thick corrupted matter.  
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is fitting at first when they appear that one makes a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, in which the point is held in the fire, or from long aristolochia root, or with a lentil cautery.  
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further ahead, but it breaks the superfluity from which they come, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut 
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great discharges of blood from the cut artery at the wound that comes to the pardefuers, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, if you hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no drop issues forth; then apply hot cauteries olive oil, several small and large ones until they are all red; then take one, large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps further when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another cautery that is in the fire. 
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to use one after the other until the blood is stopped flowing; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows freely from an artery, it cannot be well stopped immediately when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four methods that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by strong ligature with thread, or by medicines placed upon which have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and restrained tightly. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	He who will administer the stopping of bleeding by tightly binding cloths or by putting burning things upon it, or other similar things, it is of no use if it does not work.  
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he has neither mirror nor medicine at hand, he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it is numbed both on the wound and on the vein; and he must not move it, but wet it with cold water often, so that it is very cold, until the blood is frozen and thickened and numbed; and then make inquiries ahead about those whom he needs to cauterize and who need medicines. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of incision 
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is fitting to use fire cautery or burning medicines, and the uses and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have put this chapter from top to bottom, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that those who wish can find it more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this one, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than the first one on cautery, and for this reason it is necessary to be more careful. 
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there often occurs evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in treating wounds, and in extracting arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.  
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Some come who are so distressed by their illness that they die easily from the severity they find in their ailment, and from the extent of its harm; and one must fear these. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And some of them will give you their sense, and say: “Wait, I am cured”; and the illness is spiteful. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you should consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not work foolishly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take oaths; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you to acquire good renown, glory, and long memory. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	My dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what it is before or the chapter on cauteries, which I have devised from the beginning to the end so that you may more easily find what you need. 
dou chief plein d’aigue	When the head is full of sharp pain 
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too hard; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this ailment except in children, and all those I have seen hastened death; and therefore it seems to me that it is better for me to leave such treatments to others. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of sharp pain, and the head swelled each day so that it could no longer support it; and the moisture grew so much that it died, and this moisture gathered below the bone on the spine, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you cleave a wide split in the head; and let it be as long as two of us, so that the moisture runs out; and see the shape of the spatula. 
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker and the abscess larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross according to this form: 
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs you see are the corners of the head open on each side, and the sharp point jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond to you: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner: 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterward, bind the incisions with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head be straightened evenly, and give the patient dry meat from a place without moisture to eat as long as the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and the gathering of the point; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess appears, and the point of the gathering, and make a slit according to your ability; and be careful not to sever an artery; and let blood flow freely so that the patient does not die from the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	of rheum  
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there occurs in someone a sickness that is called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the breasts, and the sickness is old, and the cure of medicine does not profit, then the last resort is cautery with which one severs two arteries.  
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is fitting then, when you have seen them swell, that the patient turns his head back; afterwards rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck to the whole cloth; then look where the vein goes, and the veins of one and the other are after the ears, and they are full; then mark the veins with ink, then cut one and the other with an acute spatumile in two parts, until the size vein reaches the bone, and this is done by the breadth of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatumile below the artery and cut it above, cutting as much as you must through. 
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood leaps from above continuously. 
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not appear to the touch, it is fitting that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark with ink and cut down to the bone; and what it is fitting for blood to flow out is six ounces, and perhaps a bit more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point without pus, so that no abscess comes there, then bind the wound and dress with ointment until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	from migration 
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migration comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture from tears and the heats in the temples and the old, stubborn foreknowledge and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and all that does not profit him at all, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted. 
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient shaves the hairs from his temples and finds the artery that appears in the temple, for it appears well by its beating, and is less full than in some men who are too cold; and if it is full, then the patient ties off its neck with some cloths, then rubs the place with a coarse cloth and raises the place with hot water as long as the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the shape: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then lift it up with forceps and carefully remove the cobwebs that are beneath it from each side; and if the artery is delicate, twist it with the point of a hook, then cut off that portion according to the quantity of the two ends. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will jump out altogether without any doubt. 
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Let the blood flow for six hours to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong doubled silk thread so that putrefaction does not come before the wound heals, and there is continuous bleeding; then cut off the excess between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the ends with a hot iron until the bones are exposed so that the ends are severed; this is the milder operation, if the patient does not have a fever and he is of warm complexion. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is a help to end the humors; therefore it is of greater help against the humors. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the place with old cotton and put well-made tents on top; and when you untie them, treat them with dry medicines that produce flesh, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a section of the artery as far as you work on it, hasten to cauterize with a cautery, or apply vitriol to the place and hold it in your hand until the blood is congealed; and if you do not have this available, put your finger on the place until the blood freezes, and apply cold water to the place until the blood stops, and it will be extracted as necessary; and that which is easier and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein with a two-part trenching cautery, but let the trenchings be well spaced to maintain their heat for a longer time.  
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less of its heat. 
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives a space of one finger's width, and then when you have marked to make the incision with the two points, and you put the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two; and they be spaced apart between the two points for it is not soldered with this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery: 
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the bridge of the nose, and no medicine that is made profits him at all, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and feel his forehead trembling as if shivering; and his limbs are thin and moist so that the hairs on the papers fall out, and the papers are scorched and burned by the heat of the tears, then this cure is needed.
