Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancients “cure contuse”, and it is that you make at the back of the patient who has this disease the hairs he has on his forehead, then make him III cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as II does all down the forehead by going down to the nose, and the other II as II ribs above the papers, and beware of cutting the arteries that are at II sides above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II mandibles, and let each wound be III fingers across joined; and have ready a piece of sponge and a lot of cloths to wipe the blood, then put the spatula sharp on II sides which is the shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the II cuts at all the skin that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second, and then pull out this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first incision, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other. 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	Put the sharp side towards the flesh and the blunt side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle of the incision. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the wound so that the incision is continuous until it reaches what appears to be the heart, then make another cut in the middle of the incision until the other side; then draw out the blood equally and squeeze the area to remove the collected blood; then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put soft cloths soaked in wine, oil, and ashes on top, and watch that no abscesses form; and on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a large compress of hot water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other remedies used for treating wounds, until it is healed.  
dou reume des eulz	Where the eyes prick 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some catarrhal ailment comes habitually, and you see the eyes red and small, and weaken sight, and papers burned; and the hair falls out, or one finds a sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that this matter and this catarrh does not come only from many veins, but also the bad cure which it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And command the patient to lie on his back, then make a large cut between the forehead and the temple. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move the jaw; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then insert cotton wool between the two edges of the incision and linen thread; then bind over it cloths softened in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until it begins to char, then cure it with drying things, which cause charring. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and administer it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow all over. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the stuffing of the ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that is lodged in the ears is one of four things: either grains, or a beast, or a stone from a mine, or something similar such as iron; or seed, such as wasps, beans, peas; or something flowing, such as water and easily, and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is lodged in the ear a stone or some other kind of thing that does not adhere to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then hold the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil and then administer extraction; and make him sneeze deliberately, and stop up his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times a boil comes to a head through this treatment; and if it does not come to a head, administer extraction with fine forceps, of which this is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes to a head with the forceps, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine lancet of small double edge; and if it does not come to a head by this, make a reed of iron and push the point of the reed or hole of the ear strongly, and plug that which is around the reed with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the reed; then treat until it comes to a head, for many times it comes to a head as we have said; and if it does not come to a head in any of these ways, take some glue, such as is taken from birds, and put it on some instrument suitable for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and treat until it comes to a head.  
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not leap from all these things that we have said, quickly cut the ear like a hot abscess so it drains, and spasms; and the way of the incision is that you first bleed the patient on the head, and draw blood according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fatty part or nearby; let the incision be shaped like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is inside and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a thin, delicate spatula according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.  
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine forceps and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute pain then when the head is in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a conditional sneeze first, and stuffs the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the pain is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out forcefully through this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take several stones according to the length of your thumb, light and smooth, and heat them a little in the fire; then place one or two stones on the patient's ear, and strike it with the foot from another side, and strike another stone upon the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this from stone to stone until the pain subsides completely, and thus it will come out entirely. And if you see that, take a piece of wire and burn one end in the ear, and hold the other end in fire until the softer wire burns; then repeat with other pieces of wire until the pain subsides completely, as we have said about the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of a beast, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, use tweezers for extraction; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms embedded in the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not profit at all, it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, take them with fine tweezers, and if none appear, take a cane whose shape is as follows:  
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most subtle tip into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then gently draw out the whole cane; do this often until all the worms come out.  
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, then you stuff cotton around the worm as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven for the removal of worms, and you will find them where you treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, which are shaped as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or iron, there are three holes below the small openings, and above them are covers for distilling; and to press the distillation inside the instrument of iron well made for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap cotton around the point evenly; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see into the worm, and let the worm be in the ear; then put the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation be heated slightly over the fire so that it can be distilled into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the numbing of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults by numbing of a wound, or by a splinter driven into the ear, and this numbness sometimes comes entirely in the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes the hole bursts, and one can see it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes entirely, if one cannot see it, is a grievous ailment in many ways, and in this case it is fitting that you put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opening, then the work has all of its course, for this is its form: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind all around, so that it does not bruise the ear; if the opening is from a splinter or bone of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers, and pull it gently, until all of those splinters are removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is perfect in the ear, then take a subtle razor and lightly heat it in the fire, then put it on the flesh of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the operation where the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder on ground vitriol; and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you draw out the tent and put in another tent moistened with cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, as long as the swelling is removed; then heal it until it is cured.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop bleeding which are or are discussed in the treatment of distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paper  
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment which comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is fitting that you extend them with tongs and pincers, and cut off the head from its roots; then put on the place vitriol ground up. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not come out whole, then cauterize them with a lentil-shaped cautery, and cauterize after the incision has healed; and often they heal so that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and they do not return.  
de la gresle	of the greyscale 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come upon papers of the eyes certain things that seem rough in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "hail," and it is a gathering of large moisture on the paper above and below; the operation is as follows: take care if the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then make two cuts wide apart, and lightly scrape off the skin from each part, then take it with pincers and cut it out. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it out without piercing the paper, do not grieve for the patient; and if the fissure is large, sew the gathering together, and care for it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply any force, for ointments will restore it quickly and engender flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail descends into the inside of the ear toward the upper part, turn over the paper and grasp the hail with pincers and cut it out, pressing from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hail is cut out, wash the eye with warm salt water and treat the place so that it generates flesh until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is engendered in cloths of paper on top, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves much their eyes;
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exit among them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth and arrange a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity it contains of exit from each part, then put it on top of it; and press with your fingers on one side and the other so that the exit is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula trenching a slit about wide, and let it not be any larger than the wound one makes when opening a vein; and make the skin all around until you come to the exit; and in several positions, the exit comes from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull then the whole piece of cloth with your fingers in front and behind until it is loosened; and be careful that you do not insert into the slit anything but the whole spatula up to the eye, lest you injure it.  
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the arrowhead does not appear at the beginning of the incision, widen the incision slightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and put them on the site, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which has remained. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there comes to the site a hot abscess, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of papers 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow other than those that are natural, and they are aged, they harm them and bring about manners of diseases such as accustomed tears and softenings of the papers and albugine, so much is it a cause of the destruction of them; and the cure is according to four manners: either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is said before in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by canes, according to what I will say.  
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is fitting that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if you insert a needle along all the thread above it; and be this below the margin of the paper where the hairs grow below these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs joined, all the spatulum cutting, from the large tear duct to the small; then extract the thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and drapel, then sign upon the paper a figure of an anchor, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is fitting that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided into all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need to make a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make a mark with a pen along the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the large tear down to the small one; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs as thick as a root, then put the needle in one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all off; then join the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all fine thread, and wipe away the blood, and make the excess of threads on the two eyebrows dry by using any sticky things, if you see fit to do this; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the suture and the threads until three or four days; then cure the wound without sutures with drying and constricting things, for the paper will stick together at the healing of the wound and its joining, but the stitch is useless (as the ancients said), and this work is without fear; and if there is another way: it is that you sign the paper with a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, at three needles according to the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take what overcomes small forces equally according to the shape which is here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, and put it in the shape; and put one thread on the large tear, and the other thread on the small one, and gather between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above which you have marked, as we have recounted, then bring together the two edges of the wound by suture, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, appease it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and it sometimes happens that the hair on the paper is converted: then it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artful. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and put the thread inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two fine ligatures as long as the paper and the width of a spoon; and cut the two ends into two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of what protrudes from the paper at the eye, and tighten the two canes from the two parts formed; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin which grows will tighten and shrink and carry, as long as it seeks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, cut with force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is sutured, remove the paper, and the hair will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a subtle needle and put in it a very fine silk thread; then bring the edges together and tie them subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order on the other side another subtle silk thread quickly, and tie the ends of the two threads; then have the patient place his head on your lap; and let it be near the sun so that the work is revealed, for it is a subtle and small work, then put the needle all along the scalp at the root of the hair, and pierce the paper quickly while you draw it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the paper, and put into the paper that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out altogether with the paper along with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is removed and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the hair underneath according to the thread that you have ordered, until the hair comes out freely through the hole above it and you can see it with your eye; then you will treat the hair and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for II days or III, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long horsehair with it, let it grow with the one you leave there, until it is elongated and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacratio" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by frequent wounding, or cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you split that suture and loosen its edges, and put linen tents inside, and bind them until it is healed; and it does not suit to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or elderflower water and flaxseed are cooked, and ointments diachylon melted in any of the oils, and they wrap a tent, and cure it thus. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close according to the form it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing more than remedies for this disease so that it does not return according to the form it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	from the flesh that comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is below, which truly is called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause comes from a wound and a fissure and a cautery and similar things; and the way of doing the work in this case is that you take a needle, in which it has double thread, and put it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct as far as the right, so that the threads come out on two sides of the flesh; then spread the flesh above the entire needle, and cut at a span wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is proper, that is good; if not, then take a razor and put it into the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two fissures on either side within the paper; and let the sides of the two fissures be at the two angles of the incision which you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter that has the name "Greek I"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are below, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then give care to it as we have said of softening medicines, and dressings, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split or a suture or a cautery, it is fitting that you make a full split below the hairs of the eyelids, and according to what is said before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare everything from all their power how they can bring back the shape to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what suits them of work and instruments are in several positions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	Of the dressing of the eyelid 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens in a simpler way so that the eyelid above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor do its natural work, then it is fitting that you put the point of a razor below the eyelid, and lift it up; and hold it with tweezers, as long as you cut what is joined with a very subtle spatula, which is not too sharp nor too cutting so that the patient does not suffer because the spatula is too sharp, nor makes the eye bleed; and let your incision, with which you separate that assembly, be lightly made, so that the eyelid returns according to its natural shape; and cleanse all that assembly, and sometimes put in the salty eye wash water, and lift it with sweet water, and with rosewater; then put between the eyelid and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool soaked in plenty of egg white; and after the third day use rose water and other soothing things as long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the angle of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is according to two manners: one is nervous and resembling hard sinew, and another which is not nervous but resembling white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and believed pinched, cannot be moved; and both resemblances begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers the entire vision and all the light and movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is such that the patient puts his head in good health, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then coils the angle like pincers of small doubleure, and extends it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and stick it in the middle of the angle, and pierce it through with the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and extend it above, and shave all the hair on the side of the angle which covers the prunele and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with the whole spatula subtly and with small forces, and leave the flesh natural or tear duct so that by the incision no body of tears usually comes; and sometimes only extend the angle to the oncine and to the thread, as we have said; then the shave is done on all the spatula according to what its form is: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision put a piece of silk thread into the eye, and with a collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put in the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured by medicines; and it grows back as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light sharp piece according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail subtly above it, and if you see that it diminishes a little and the rasping presses it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and a red collar and silk thread, and stop up the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.  
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first heal the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear duct harms the eye greatly, suspend it with a thread, and cover one part and not all at once so that tears do not flow; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the iris  
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the iris, restricting it on the eyelids, and looking like a rose of coral; and the operation is such that the patient puts his head in a sound position, then operates the eye, cutting off all that flesh with suitable pincers for this purpose, and holding it tight; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting it with a razor until the end, taking care not to damage the eye during the operation; and let the incision be where the spatula is, as we said in the incision of the nail and with small force so that one removes the scab, just as the form after this chapter demonstrates it; and when the incision is finished and all the flesh is removed, apply to the eye oil of cedar crushed or you distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put on hot cotton with egg white on the eye, so that it is assured against a hot abscess; and if there remains something, and the pain overwhelms you and you doubt a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and do this as long as any flesh appears in the eye by this means. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you relieve the cure of each weak from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member suffers from the work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered over the eye, and tolerate to sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary therefore that you first look at whether the eye is in which there is swelling, and if there are no other diseases except the swelling; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins at every incision according to his wisdom, and let the incisions be subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there shall be two incisions by degrees in the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one must carefully cut those veins subtly and wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins removed from the eye;
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot draw out all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the eye with things that soothe its pain, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and the hot abscess is secure, then begin again according to this manner which is before until he is healed; and this is the way of strength: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and with burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, there is something in it that you must cleave open on the abscess, where it should run, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.  
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all the instruments of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief," and is made of very hard iron at its head end, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a bit so that you know that corruption is healed; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the edges are soldered and flesh grows and the body of the bowel is soldered and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not reopen nor become abscessed, and no bad accidents occur, know that it is healed; if not, there is nothing else to do but to return the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this method: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with an iron and with sharp medicines; and when it is uncovered, take the drill according to this method, and let the head of the iron be at three angles and let the shaft be tapered down to the point as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and remove your hand from the eye so that you touch it, then return to the whole drill until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the vein comes there if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the places, the matter goes to the cheek; this is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no disturbance in the nose, nor decrease, it is necessary to tie the patient; then you heal him, then apply cupping glasses or a cautery without cutting to suck, then put on the eye a poultice made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity the eye needs; then strain it from above with a hard bandage, and start the cupping glasses again to suck without cutting; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the strained eye day and night, and if the poultice softens, it is necessary to strain it very much; then remove the poultice after a day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not; start the poultice and cloths and bandage and cupping glasses again until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For the tearing of linen cloth 
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the linen cloth, then it opens, and there come forth papers as if it were resin grain, and it is easy to see; then if you wish to cover it, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the part below up to that above. Then thrust another needle where the doubled thread is in the part of the tear; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position; then grasp the place of the doubled thread and tie one part of the linen around it, and draw it tight, then pull out the needle and put on the eye a moistened linen cloth steeped in egg white; and leave it until the threads grow together with the linen, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the linen on every side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great inflammation, pierce it with a fine lancet that comes straight from the fire, and drain the watery humor and reduce the inflammation, and then extract the arrow as soon as it is healed. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the gut of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the gut assembled in the eye, resembling a sharp descent, and it is not sharp; and the manner of its appearance is such that you have the patient sit on a suitable and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on two sides, and move it until you see the gut come up to your eyes; then be it stuck, and do not descend and be covered with light, and see the patient's things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is sharp, and if the descent of the gut is not equal as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and strike on the cornea with a continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, distill into sharp hot oil mixed with honey or sharp fenugreek boiled with honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healed.  
des aigues de l’oil	Of the sharp oil 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the resemblances of the sharp ones in the division, and what it is necessary to pierce; so work according to healthiness. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, far from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of oil to your left hand if the eye is on the left, or to your right hand if the eye is on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is on the left, the instrument which is called “almagda,” or in your left hand, if the eye is on the right; then put the point of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray in that white part of the eye to the side of the smaller tear duct; then push the instrument which is called “almagda” virtuously and turn your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that the “almagda” reaches the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of the “almagda” be at the perfection of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, then put the instrument up to where the sharp part is, then press it down one path after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it stings now, let the patient see it in front of them and the instrument in their eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a little rest, and if the sting goes back up the second time, put force on it with the instrument, and when it is stuck in and it does not rise, pull out the almond slightly while turning your hand bit by bit; and then put it back in with a little piece of sel gemme, and lift the eye from within. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in the oil soaked wadding or linen moistened in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and tie it with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, we and those who are of our time, put a common poultice on top with plenty of egg yolk. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes that are too hard, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberet," of which this is the form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then put in almond paste, as we have said; 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, untie the eye before the seventh day, and dress it with what soothes abscesses; and when it is soothed, untie the bandage and put a poultice of orilliet on its face to cover it for a few days, and let it be in that dark room. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then let it come out of the house little by little, and let it return to its state; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	One came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in some foreign lands they made a kind of almond paste, with which one sucked up sharp objects, but however I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almond paste, so that those who do not know them may recognize them; and they are made of grain properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the last one in three sharp angles. 
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh near the nose  
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or near the nose fleshy growths of various kinds, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there are such growths with flesh tinged with purple color, and if there is flesh with fair complexion. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore for those of these growths which are fair and not inflamed, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and put a small lancet to those growths, and cut them deeply; then take what you can hold with a sharp spatula on one side until you know that this growth is entirely removed.  
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that you cannot take hold of, then work at it all with subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if it swells or becomes an abscess, cut it as is fitting; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood is dried up and all the growths are removed, then put vinegar mild and sharp or wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the newborn's work, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh near the bone above, which the instrument cannot reach to cut: then it is necessary that you put a thread of linen a little thick, and tied by hand at intervals, and have between each knot a space of one finger or less; and put the child's cheek on the thread in his nose at its lowest point, and pull it while smelling so that it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times children are made thus at school, and it is a light thing for those who want to do it; then hold the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after the other as we who are on the thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the flesh has been corrupted by it, then draw the thread, wipe away the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose just as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put a cane of lead in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, into which oils and medicines are distilled. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or steel, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and conduct it in the same way; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and it has a handle on the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquor. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh take the birth 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a sickness is born at the head near birth which is called "telul" and grows and becomes large until it is visible; and for this reason you must cut it at the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put on the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of purple color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron for it is an ulcerated abscess; for when one cuts it sometimes great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not purple in color, and you see that one can cut all of it, empty the patient and cut without fear, and heal the place with drying and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the birth is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
