It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two edges at a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you flay all the parts of their core until they bleed, then assemble the two edges at a suture, and remove it, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and powdered incense; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is such that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have shown you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes there are hard abscesses within the lips, resembling grains of millet, both small and large; then it is fitting that you turn back the lips and make a cut on each one, and take them with tweezers and cut in every part; then apply the place afterwards with powdered vitriol, until the blood is dried up; and then wash with water, and dress the place with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums  
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there grows on the gums fleshy growths, which the ancients called "albulus"; then it is fitting that you hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood drain; then put on the place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if this flesh returns after the incision, and it often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery. And these are the shapes of instruments for cutting.  
des sordens	of deafnesses 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and citron and worm-eaten, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are stinking; so it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your lap, and raise the teeth or the scabs where they appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do with the blackness and the greenness, and with the jaundice and the other stains, until they are cleansed; and if one removes that which is at the first reason, it is good; if not, one begins again on the second day and the third, until you have raised everything; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to raise, according to what the work shows, because the razor with which one raises the teeth has other shapes than those with which one raises between the teeth; and these shapes and others be prepared with you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay the pulling as much as you can, for this one must not do; because it is a very high substance until then we have no excuse for pulling. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you are certain of the aching tooth. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks that it is a sound tooth, and pulls the good tooth; and nevertheless, the pain does not depart because of this, until the bad one is pulled out, for we have often wanted to do this with these saints; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth at all its gum edge very strongly in order to hold back the gums from all sides; then move it to your two hands or hold it with subtle tongs at the first touch and touch, until it is well loosened, then grip it firmly with the tongs; and have the head of the patient between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take any of these instruments and insert it gently into each side, and move it as you did before. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, it is fitting that you fill it with cloths where the holes are; and if you extract it subtly with forceps so that it does not break when extracted; and it is very wise to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and the evil of the root returns to the patient with greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to do as ignorant healers do who, through their haste and boldness, sometimes break the jawbone and do not apply what we have said; but they bring about a great disease through the roots that remain or the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.  
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, with which one can pull teeth first, should be long pointed and have large handles so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are their forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large members so they do not bend when pulling, and let them be of well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the molars. 
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is fitting that you put on the place cotton moistened with butter for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the gums are softened, then put in the tongs which are called "algefri", with which the head seems like a bird's beak; and let them be made inside like a file and this is the form:  
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, it is fitting that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a chisel, of which this is the form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps because of this, it is good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two prongs, of which here is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are in front in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, of which here is the form: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments with teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and subtle wise masters invent by themselves their instrument according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others, so that one does not break a chariot or other bones, or where it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit it, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-gripping to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, if you have all these instruments: 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to the body's natural form and the shape is ugly, and especially in virgin women, you should know if the tooth grew after the other teeth and is not in its proper place and cannot be filed or smoothed: then a saw; and if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and is made of sharp steel at the tip: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the saw cuts little by little in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, take a file of this kind, whose shape is like this: 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth little by little in your hands lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks off; then smooth it at the end with no razor, and if the point is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens  
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth loosens, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without it hurting, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and that does not work; then you must restrain it with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see to straighten the teeth, take the thread and wrap it twice between the two sound teeth, then put the loose tooth between those teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach wisely up to the other sound tooth; then begin the wrapping again up to the part where you started, and pull your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.  
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the bone with pliers and join them together, and place it between sound teeth so that it does not damage the tongue; then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens or the threads break, remove it with another thread. If it remains and serves in this manner for its entire duration, this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two missing ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the head of the tooth has been replaced, one puts it back in its place, time and again, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes a tooth shape from a cow's bone, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and removes it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes below the tongue by nature, or one is born with it; or by accident of a sewn wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is due to a sewing of a wound, then insert the hook and cut widely that ligament; and guard that the incision be not too deep, because of the artery which is below; and when you have done this, apply a poultice of rose water and honey, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a linen bandage; and bind the patient every night, so that the wound may not heal. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding, apply powdered vitriol to the place; and if it does not stop, cauterize it with a lentil-shaped cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is leaning towards blanching, and there is moisture, cut into it with a fine scalpel, and free it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding does not stop in your work, apply powdered vitriol until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the pus; then lift the place from around and below, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there comes inside the throat boils which are called "godath," and properly they are called the two almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is an abscess hard of small sense and dark color, do not touch it at all with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it at all with iron, also for the draining of blood; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will cut it, or it would burst by itself; and if it is of a whitish color, and the root is thin, have ready the instrument to cut, but first look whether the abscess has subsided and is calmed. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his chest should be in your light, and open his mouth and take the serjans between your hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, so it is the shape; and it should be of silver or a thin iron as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press your tongue against all these instruments, and you will see the abscess. Then take the lancet and put it into the almond, and hold it strongly above that as much as you can; and do not drag any cloth along with it, then apply the instrument to the spot, which is shaped so that it seems like one force; and even though the tips are bent and one against the other, they are very sharp, and it is made of hardened iron or steel. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, then apply the forceps, which are shaped like this:  
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And they are sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have grasped one of the almonds, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water that is both hot and easy to swallow, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water in which pomegranate rind has been cooked or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped. Then treat it until it is healed; and if at any time other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, then treat them as you did the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say, an abscess of small sense; and it had nearly closed the whole throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was stopped up, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained so for one day or two. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two reins through the two holes from which it was born.  
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then and put in one oncine, then I drew it out, and drew out a large portion of bowel; then I did the same through the other hole from which it was born, and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I put the oncine into that abscess, and extracted some of it, and only a drop of blood came out; and thus the passage of the throat was opened for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut away from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again, and fill up the place which I had emptied, until it became very large; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.  
de l’uve	from the eye 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When a cold descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called “perpendicular”; and if it is below large and round, it is called “eye”. 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the boil below is quieted, and it is subtle, then it is fitting that you cut it; and the one which is round gathered and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a yellow color or black, then it is fitting that you make an incision in it.  
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore it is fitting, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument of which we have made mention before; then put the lancet in the eye, and draw it underneath, and cut it with one or two instruments as I have said in the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid to be cut, it is necessary that you use something soothing for the fear of cauterization. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery must be sharp and pointed. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient put his head on your lap, and then press the tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and confiscate with a sharp pointed tip so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and employ the covering of this instrument, which is as follows: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And say if the head has hair where you put the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that his saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not go down the throat and the bleating; then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, until you see it soften and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton in the pipe above, until the cotton burns on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and cut afterwards after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, if you restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water, and cure it with gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and put it on the fire and boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and have an instrument inserted into the pot according to this method: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And let it be of silver or iron, and let one of the ends be put in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through a tube, until the eye is mortified; then begin again often, until the eye dries up, and make sure that you do not do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a spoonful of egg so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the spoonful of egg will not make the steam heavy in the mouth, and this is good treatment along with safety. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else gets stuck in the throat; so it is necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if it pulls out the stuck thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of stale bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will come loose, and then you will pull it out forcefully; and if it does not come out forcefully from what we have said, take an instrument of a plunger according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be bent at its head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head raised upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all breath leave him, nor push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is airy; if he swallows it down, or he draws it back with the whole instrument equally, as far as it may be drawn. 
de la sansue de la gorge	from the dryness of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is the dryness, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not profit, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you have pressed his tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the dryness, draw it out entirely with a small hook, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a cane with hair, and put it in the throat of the sick person, then push or drive the end of the cane with a hot iron, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient suffers from acute pain every day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it down in a gulp, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as he feels the pain, spit it out. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he does not spit it out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I described for fumigating the eye; do this many times, for it will fall out without hesitation.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is this: you take a pot with live coals, and place it covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and the head of the instrument is put through this hole; then pour in your fumigation, and have the patient put the head of the cane into his mouth, and close his mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes all the way to the pain; and the pain will now fall out. And if it does not spit out, start the fumigation again many times; let the patient feel thirsty, and eat salty and similar things, and do not drink water; then he will need it to come out through this method.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats a fistula is such that when one can see it, it resembles tongs bent to be inserted into the throat; and it has the appearance of the beak of a falcon, and it has the roughness of a file so that what it takes hold of, it cannot let go; and see here its form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses. 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many types of abscesses are, according to what memory brings here from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners by which the first is in its own appearance, and the second by what it holds moisture.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is by the places where they are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different than those of the fundament, and abscesses of fleshy places are different than those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are mature, and they do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it as long as it is ripe enough, there is a chance that the ligament and nerve of the joint will be corrupted, by which this is a cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is near the fundament, pierce it even if it is ripe; and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess that is ripe without complete digestion, except for the one that is near the fundament, so that it becomes fully ripe, and elongated within, and a fistula comes; and it cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is death according to its fulfillment, and it is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where there is more dependence on the place of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the perforation be the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all its equals where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that weep, according to that member. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, if it moves, you should leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of it, the body will be lengthened by the venom from it, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and its depths will harden. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb may need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting that you administer small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become as yellow as cloths, and is dead, then it is fitting to do as one does for buboes: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and if there are those which are cut as the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the groin; and if there are those where one makes a rounded incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.  
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial boil, it is necessary that you pierce it fully; and it is necessary when the boil is large, and it has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then stop up the boil until the next day, then draw out something further; do this many times at intervals, until all the pus comes out; in the same way if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits sometimes leap with the discharge of the pus, and by chance the patient may die, and you do not blame yourself. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your boil, if wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the boil is small; and if it is a full incision, apply tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large boil, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the boil a part of the skin, and you have sewn it around, it is necessary to fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then unbind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and quickly soak a cloth and place it on the bleeding area many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply a bandage and dressing, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter time, and the wound or abscess is very sensitive, then you should put soaked cloths and bandages moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is summertime, and the wound is fleshy, then you should put soaked cloths moistened with cold water and oil, or wine and cold oil, for three days as we have said; and then untie the abscess, wipe it clean and treat it as needed, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is important to know generally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter. 
des soros	of the sores 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where boils come in small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in cloths, as the joiner of a hinge, and very much there are resemblances. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some fatty and such where there is moisture as well as pus; and if there are such that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt whether the artery does not make contrary.  
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist so that you prove all the instrument which is called "introducer," from which the form comes hereafter, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it pass through above with length. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is voided, so flay without leaving any skin which contains that moisture, for it returns again when one leaves nothing; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will run what remains from the night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the dressing again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it will not dislocate at night; then heal the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds onto thick pus, do it according to this form, lengthwise; and put your ointments on it, and scarify it from all sides, and put all your treatment of drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I have told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for an abscess if it is piercing, and in the loin and thigh as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting into a piercing abscess and moistening it is lighter, because they are of little blood.  
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or boils have no moisture, and like those boils that I cut open in the head of an old woman; and I found the boil as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had struck any, they would have done as much harm as striking a stone.  
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses coming or chief, except those that come at the nape of the necks and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the lowest place, so that pus can flow out; and the treatment as it is fitting. 
des scrophules	For scrofula  
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just as the nodule and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the likenesses of these scrofula are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others so malignant that they will not obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then which you see of good disposition to touch, and is like in color to the flesh, and moves from each part and is not adherent to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; it is fitting that you cut it above, and scrape it from each part, and extend the two lips of the core with pincers if you need them, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut a nerve nor a vein, and let the scalpel be neither too dull nor sharp, so that your hand does not slip, and do not see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.  
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and remove the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed and the wound softened, and begin to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work until you complete it; then look with your index finger if any small scrofula remains, and cut them and clean them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not right that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.  
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the whole scrofula, it is fitting that you bring together the two edges of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no longer any superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	Then it is fitting that you understand how to cut out the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula that retain superfluity, pierce them where it appears dead; and pierce it as the one previously mentioned, in a hanging manner, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, cure it with ointment drawing flesh, until it is healed.  
de squinance	of squint 
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit in the throat which is called "epiglottis" be scraped; and this should not be done by anyone, for all the veins and the lung of the patient are at risk for those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the canal of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from choking. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we split it below three circles or four, a small slit across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from inquiring.  
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is fitting that he extends the skin of the throat to the entire incision, then splits the heart until it reaches the trachea; and removes blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cuts the windpipe, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the lung which escapes through the broken place, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all alone without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely torn open, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the windpipe is severed. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and heal it, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden take a knife and stab it into her throat, cutting away part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and even though she had not covered her throat or any vein except for the throat, the veins were cut by the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and sewed the wound and treated it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the young woman except that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterward to her normal state; for this reason I say that there should be no fear in cutting the epiglottis. 
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess of a yellowish color, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; in the natural kind there is no cause.  
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind occurs in two ways, of which one is similar to fat boils, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us by artery; and there is danger, and it does not suit to work with hot iron except in those that are small, and you should try and explore all the passage: if you find it as soft as new fat, and it cannot be drained at any vein, then cut it, as one cuts boils, and treat it all its length; if there is any, then bind it well immediately, and cure it as is proper until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	from us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which we are, of which I will say all the resemblances; and now it behooves me to say all the difference that is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting as long as the boiling is not passed, and is fulfilled the putrefaction; then rests the fever and the heat. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With swelling there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which are its own sac and are according to the color of the body, and begins as a pea, and grows large; and they are according to two resemblances, either greasy or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It behooves, when you come to the treatment of swelling, that you expect and inquire first with all the instrument that is called “introducer,” according to what its form will come or chapter that is after.  
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses of us is that you take the wettest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the center; then do this according to the size of the abscess; then extract the trocar, and take care lest it jump out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs out, whatever color it may be, do as I have said for the other abscesses; and if after the trocar no moisture comes, know that it is fatty; then make an incision in a cross shape, take it with forceps, and lightly scrape it on each side and keep the skin where it lies so that you draw it healthy with the new; and if you cannot draw it healthy, draw it by pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there for nothing, the nerve returns many times; and if one part remains, and it does not grieve you, apply the wound with some corrosive sharp powders, and remove the wound, and put soothing things on hot abscesses, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nerve is large, cut the two edges of the wound, and cure it from what causes flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats contrary to you or another hastens and apply the place of ground vitriol, and leave it there for II days or III, as long as the wound rots, and calms the ebullition with blood; then return to cover what remains in the nerve.  
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the inserting instruments, and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three manners: large, medium, and small, to surround fistulas abscesses; and they are also like needles with which we cut the scabs, and they are of citrine steel, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more and are better tested with black lead to surround the curves of fistulas; and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of lancets are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets which have two curves in three ways also; and there are lancets which have three curves, and are also of three ways; and there are lancets which have two curves, and lancets of one curve only, and are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some which do not cut very deeply except on one side, with which one scrapes the skin, so that one does not sever the vein nor the nerve; and of these instruments are the small alembics held in the hand, so that the patient does not notice them when opening abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument resembling a flaying knife according to this form with which one cauterizes blood.  
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place where it heals alongside veins and arteries, and never again according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes men's breasts swell when they begin to rot, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must do so according to the form of this line .b. up to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine containing charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs low and is softened due to its size as it happens in women, then cut it into two ribs above, through two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or because of blood flow, then you must fill the wound with softened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it draws out the remaining fat, then treat it until it is healed.  
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come below the armpits are ways of hard scrofula where it has ribs, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment suitable for this until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofula, then make it as we have said in the clefts of scrofula, and if the wound runs pus, apply a cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	of the breaking of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.
