When the artery is broken and the skin above it is sewn together, many times abscesses form, and the same happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and if the knower knows when it is for the artery, then the abscess is long and straight; and when you feel it at your fingertips, you feel it pulling away; and when it is for the vein, it is round and appears deflated; and it is foolish to open this abscess, even when it is under the armpits and the angles or the neck and many other places, and it is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to avoid the use of iron instruments, and the one who is in charge must also avoid it; and in the one who is swollen from a broken artery that runs under the skin for a long distance; then make an incision as on acorns, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed; then put a needle under it and let it pierce through to the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then point the place between the two ligatures with a retractor until the pus that is in it comes out, and let the abscess be released; then apply a dressing soaked in wine, as long as the ligatures hold; then treat it with anointments suitable for this, until it heals; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, you should hold in your hand what you can of the abscess along with all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you are holding in your hand, and let it pierce through, and have a double thread so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you, or tie one of the two ends of the thread to the two ligatures; and if you doubt that the threads will come loose, put another needle on all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and extract the threads in four places; then open the abscess so that the excess comes out, then remove the excess from the core and leave what is tied; then apply a bandage moistened with wine and oil, and then administer dressings and ointments until it heals.  
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in arteries and veins, abscesses come to nerves when they are strained, or by too much work, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and in the arms and in all their joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and is in several positions without pain; and when it is extracted, the patient feels pain, and it is not similar to the rest of the body, but beneath the heart; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor below nor above; and that which is in the joints should not be cauterized with iron: for fear it might cause contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a scalpel. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with forceps and cauterize it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it from a hook, and scarify it, then the bone-setter sets the wound together with stitches, and cures it until it is healed.  
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else a swelling, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has a subtle root, and thick head; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had small roots, and they were easily split open, and they constantly oozed moisture.  
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found that one weighed eighteen ounces and the other six ounces, and the works in incision are such that if you look and see if the patient is moist, and the color of the articulation is white and damp and has a subtle root; if you cut it with a scalpel broad, and have the cautery ready.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often comes excessive bleeding of blood, and if it does not stop, then use a cautery; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with the iron, take a thread of flax well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then loosen it, and do not cease to pull the flax thread until the artery bursts and bleeds through it without effort; and if the roots are large, be afraid to burst them immediately because of the belly, but you may well burst half, then cauterize so that they do not grow back; then treat the wound, and make sure that you do not burst the tendon which is of a dark color and poor and milky in appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerous abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards.  
quant li boude ist fuer	when the arm is strong 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the arm comes from cautery of wound or from a fissure of sinew, and is on the belly and in any one of its hollows as it happens with other wounds, or from blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what is before it, or from windiness;
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is because of the intestine's issue, then it is more diverse, and when you press on its sides it rises up, and then returns, and by chance if it is tightened, it enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and through great work. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is because of moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, and do not constrain it; and if it is because of blood, it appears by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is because of windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the works are such that you look whether its appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then it is necessary that you leave the cure. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be extended all straight, then sign a ring all around the buttock; then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with the whole spatula, then extend the half of the abscess above with the whole large hook; then bind it around with strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot be loose; then work the half of the abscess extended upon the ligature, and put your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligature, untie it, and put out the intestine from the hollow of the belly; and if you find the bowel, take it with the hook, and cut off the superfluity; and if an artery opposes you, or a vein, go around well then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two needles around what you have made in a cross so that you make pierce through; then draw the abscess in four places upon the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it ripens, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you cut it off when it becomes subtle and rotten, then cure the place with what is fitting, and close the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place with what is fitting, and sew up the place.
dou chancre	about a sore 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of a sore, and how one must work by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and say that the sore spreads into the flesh, and great caution to take in its cure, and they say the ancients that when sores are in a place where one can shave it as a sore that is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, and one must remove all of it when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not behoove you to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone ever healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in a place where one can remove it as we have said, is that you purge the patient several times of black bile; then make him sweat if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; then shave your ointments or sores, and the hair from all sides, and bone from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and squeeze the area with your hand or something else, and if the running of blood prevents you from making an incision on the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.  
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only erupted; and one should not touch with iron in these two resemblances: namely, tympany and hypoarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you treat this resemblance of dropsy which is called "erupted" with medicine, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is strong and healthy, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lay the patient straight on your hands, and have his attendants press the belly at the end by pushing the water to the lowest part of the buttock, then take the spatuled iron according to this form:  
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cutting of two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	A point, and in no way let it be so inserted that it can reach the intestines when you put it in, and cannot pierce; then look if the dropsy is gathered toward the intestines: if it must be that you split inside of the belly three finger-widths straight down above the navel; and if the dropsy is for the disease of the liver, let your incision be on the left side of the belly three finger-widths; and if it is for the spleen, let it be on the right, and it must not be that the patient lies upon the incision so that superfluities do not flow to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand to all the spatule between the skin and the fascia as much as in scraping a quantity of one nail or so; then pierce the fascia until the spatule comes to the eighth place, and this is the place of the sharp point, then draw it out, and push in this instrument of which here is the form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a subtle silver cane, and is of iron or light artichoke, and has at the lower part a small hole; and on one side, III holes; and II on another side; and I on another; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the form of the incision with which scribes cut the quill: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it now descends onto the instrument; empty it therefore by half or a third part, for if you empty it more than what is necessary at that time, the patient may die through the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or his flesh may decay, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held by the heart which stops the hole that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering, and treat the point a small quantity; do this each day, and beware of forcing as long as there remains but a drop of point.  
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and you leave a great deal of pus in him, then treat it with burial earth or hot sand, and by a great deal of sweating or bathing and sunning, and have him drink; and treat it with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the pus, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the amputation of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, as soon as possible, pierce it all the way through with a very fine instrument according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a fine tube of lead on the opening, and tie it and keep it like that for three or four days; and when he wants to urinate, remove the tube so he can urinate, and then replace it; and if it is necessary, for the urine that comes out will not let it stay closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose anus is small, if it is treated with a lead plumb, as we have said, it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have their anus in its place are crippled, for none are born who have the anus at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; and they cannot impregnate because the matter cannot come up to the marrow, and this is a grievous illness. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, then extends the head of the penis and cuts it as thick as a quill, so that the anus falls in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, have it stopped by whoever stops blood, and heal the wound until it is healed.  
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these pimples come to the penis, and they are an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; it is fitting that you take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and cleanse them all, then put soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on them; then treat them with diafinicon ointment until they are healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the pimple is malignant, of foul color and discharging pus, it is fitting that you apply a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the pimple is at the top of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is fitting that you remove the pimple that is inside first; and when that is healed, then treat it outside.  
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if the head of the penis is not well secured so that it is not pierced, blackness and corruption come to its penis and testicles; it is fitting to remove all that is black and corrupted, then bind an adhesive plaster made from honey and flour, which is made from pomegranate rind and vinegar, on top of it, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways together: that is to say, in the flow of blood and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you draw or conduct from the penis a cane of lead, and piss the patient among; and when the hair burns at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens for a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scarify with a sharp instrument the head, so that the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is a grievous thing to devise this, it is necessary that you scarify with a spatulated instrument some spots on the head of the penis and on the skin; then separate well between them, and put a thin linen cloth softened in cold water, so that it does not burn directly.  
de la circoncision	of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a severance of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless when we do this work of our own volition, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for safety. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greater part of masters and healers who did circumcision used a knife around one finger, and with force, and at all a very sharp point; it was dangerous because there are two layers, and by chance if you cut one above and the other below remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is double, and with the cleansing which is of one layer, assurance of the tip of the member is not secure; and with the cleansing of the other layer by chance the iron slips, and ruins the work, and many times they are born such that they need no cleansing, and I have seen it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	I have found the goodness of experience in modifying what is made at all points of the thread because the forces cut justly as well above as below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in one direction as long as the thread is well twisted around the leather; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing anything but tying the thread around the penis just so; then let him rejoice in all the ways that you can; then let him stretch out between your hands straight up, and point the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow at the heart, and draw it up as high as the head of the penis is drawn in; then cleanse it well of the dirt that has accumulated there, then tie the marked spot with a double thread, then tie it below the one spot to the other tie; and hold it with two fingers by the second tie to the scrotum and the index finger, and cut between the two ties; then quickly remove the heart above it and draw the head of the penis; then let the blood run drop by drop, for it is good for healing; and put powder on top and over the powder lay a cloth glued with half an egg cooked soft with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for wound cleansing is this: the two jaws should be held tightly and sharp, and the jaws should also be as large as the handle equally. 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in wound cleansing is when the core inside escapes at the incision; so it behoves you to extend it to your fingernail, just as the pus of an abscess forms; and the cup equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, take it with tongs, and then cut. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is under the foreskin is swollen, leave it until the abscess that has formed is appeased, and lightly scrape it; cut as much as you can move, and be careful of the part of the foreskin, lest it should harm anything. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the place of things within a wound with powder, as we have said in our treatise on powders, and if you cut out the core too much, and it goes above, it will do no harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	For the retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to stone, or congealed blood, or bowel, or flesh tumor, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released and you see the retention is due to a stone which is at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bent upon his knees; and his feet are placed on his back and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient so that he does not move as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards so that urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which this is the form: let it be made of fine silver, light and pointed like a bird's feather; and let the tube be a palm and a half long, and fine at the tip. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of removing urine is such that you take a double thread and tie at its head a bit of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until the bladder is empty, and this is not done according to this order unless the one who guides it where it goes is crooked; then pull the thread at all its wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then draw it out, and let the urine flow; and start again with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see sharp things and medicines distilled into it, then make use of all the instrument which is called a "clepsedre", and this is its form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the length of its neck so that the medicine passes easily into the urethra without additional trouble, so one can draw out the moisture, and put it in when needed; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and pull the string which is inside; if you pull the moisture with the catheter, and then push the string firmly inside; the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of a subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: it is as follows: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the ligaments attach. Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture which you see to be used for clysters into it, then tie it between the two breasts with a good strong double thread, and heat the pot with that moisture over the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the penis, then hold your hand on the bladder so all the moisture comes out, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it and pierce it round about; then put a strong thread through those holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a shield, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone and its extraction with medicines; and we have said the difference between a lodged stone and those that are loose, and all the signs, and in which stones one should work with a cut; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and its sign is that sharp urine comes from the bladder, seeming thin and subtle; and it makes a crackling sound, and pains the patient's penis, and bends him many times, and then stiffens; and at most of these times, there are drippings; and healing is easier for children until they are four years old, and it is a great affliction for the elderly, and it is moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and it is easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often obstructs the search for the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and pull them and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from there higher up; then make him sit between your hands evenly spaced, and his hands should be below his thighs so that the bladder is entirely sloping downwards; then seek it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to cut above the stone.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not budge at all when touched, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and insert it into its bottom, and seek the stone; and when you feel it on your finger, hold it at the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger and bring it outside where you see to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend the testicles upward with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then he inserts the scalpel cutting, of which this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And he cuts between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two hands should be right there or at the fundament, and let the incision be long so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance press if the hand which is at the fundament, so that it comes out easily without work; and know that there are stones which have angles, and edges: if it is rough it is difficult to extract; and if there is a part which is below, resembling a bean, and round, from which the exit is easy. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	Therefore, when there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you extract it with tongs which are also like a file at the head, to pull out the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it a subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot engage it thus, enlarge the hole or opening, and if the sand cuts, dissolve it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, put the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull hard, and the smaller ones afterward if there are several. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it is necessary to suture it and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the veins cannot be sutured; but nevertheless, you must strive to draw it out, or to break it up with tongs, as long as you draw it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put a softened cloth on top soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then place the patient on his back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it arises very well in the place of oil and water, then apply a dressing of diachylon ointment and basil ointment until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses should come in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and it is retained by them so that the urine is not passed normally: then put your finger into the wound and draw out the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and rot it; then lift the wound with water and alum and salt, and help it in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour when you treat it, you bind its two thighs together, and apply the medicines on top. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the passage of the penis, stuck fast so that the urine cannot pass; then apply the treatment that I have said before, cutting it many times, for this remedy excuses the incision because of this treatment. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried this. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron forceps according to this form and let it be fixed at three angles in the fire. 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the forceps into the shaft lightly until it reaches the stone; and turn the forceps in your hand against the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone on the other side; then urine will soon come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is quickly broken and comes out with the urine, then the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then cut the shaft near the stone between the two threads, then extract it, untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood from the wound; and treat it until it is healed.  
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to uncover herself to be examined, especially when she is chaste.  
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who knows well this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more deeply embedded than the stone of man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if these necessities arise, then it behooves you to take a midwife who knows well, and at pains one finds her, and if you do not find her, then take a chaste woman subtle in mind; and present her with a wise counsel in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of this art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then it behooves you to put your finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should constrain it under her finger, and recommend that she put her finger or with the sick woman, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it bit by bit from the entrance of the bladder down below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then place it upon the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is most easily moved, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her leg above the stone or below, and make the incision first small; then put the knife into the incision, if you feel the stone press hard on the wound so that the stone can come out forcefully, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have horns.  
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the resemblances to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the bleeding comes, put crushed vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of a stone from men to help you in your work; and if the bleeding comes, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put powder on the spot and bind it with bandages, and do not begin again with this one, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient die by chance; then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the pain subsides, then return to your work, as long as the stone endures. 
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white tissue, which is below the heart of the testicles and contains the egg; it is called “syfac”, and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg if one thinks it to be another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white tissue that we have mentioned. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia comes from weakness which arrives at the testicles and spreads that matter. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is yellowish, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is white tissue as we have said, it is a ripe abscess, a long pus-filled sac as the shape of an egg, and does not expose the testicles because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very fabric, then the abscess rejoins with a part of the egg white, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg white; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sinew, then he feels it well. Therefore, when you see the color of the moisture, test all the instruments thoroughly, of which the form is described above. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then, which comes after the instrument, judge what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be cleansed according to our power and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on something a foot high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the instrument to one of the two ribs near the heart of the testicles; then take the scalpel, sharp and clean, and cut through the skin of the testicle lengthwise down to the point, and make your incision straight by separating the skin of the testicle up to the white sinew, and delicately scrape it according to our power; then pierce the sinew full of sharp fluid with a large opening, and extract all the fluid, and then put on your ointments, and stretch the sinew upwards; and do not touch the heart of the testicle, but only the sinew; cut everything or in pieces immediately along its side, for if you do not cut it wisely, the fluid will return; and if the egg slips out during your work, put it back in place when you have completed the work on the sinew; then join the two lips of the heart of the testicle with a suture, then treat it as other wounds until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, doubting the flow of blood; then cut off the scrotum at all the suspensory parts, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the artery is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and put another linen moistened in wine and oil on top of the two scrotums, and put double cloths on top, and tie it all up according to this form:  
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and use them of charpie wool according to this resemblance and let them be joined together by stitching at the throat of the breeches, and one of the legs takes up on the fundament up to the back, and the other at the part where the dagger is; and the other two chief ones on the two angles, and let all the restraint be assembled in the loop of the breeches; and never medicine this branch with a cautery instead of an iron size, and it is that you take a subtle cultellar cautery, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white fascia containing the artery is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that fascia at one time, and cauterize it with this subtle hot cautery:  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in all the ways that you can, so long as you root out everything; and keep the fire from touching the egg; and know that this work is safer; while guarding against hemorrhage of blood, and gentler than the works of cutting; and if anything opposes you, or abscess boils or hemorrhages of blood or something else, then cure what opposes you, according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then perform a puncture, as I tell you, and know that when you are well certain by the signs we have said that the stagnant water is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess below at all the septum width large, and place the puncture as long as the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the pus may flow out; then put cotton on the place and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining pus, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to escape at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a pen or an instrument with which one treats the pus of dropsy, of which the form is described before; and widen the opening of the wound, and know that the pus will return and gather after six months or so; and when it has gathered as before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the testicles 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this branch, fear leads to many complications, which is why it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about its work and the similarities of an abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that many abscesses come from the body and especially the testicles; and this is very common. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know that abscesses come from an excess of sour and sharp humor which spreads to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not cause pain, but it is a troublesome abscess; and by chance there are painful, hard, and stinking abscesses with a bluish color; and sometimes they come from a new artery or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a new artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it should not be touched. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of a vein swelling is known by his disposition to the expression through the touch of the two fingers, and one can well make the incision upon this resemblance, and upon the other humors; and it is that you cut the heart of the testicles, then lift up the egg, and draw the cord from the white sheath, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already joined with these humors which are there, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is airy in the sheath or in those who are within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension, and cut around. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the humor is or its place behind, then it is necessary that you cut all of it and extract the egg as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, apply a dressing of wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped in a wrapping similar to a boil, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient grieves when he walks; and the cure for this disease is as dangerous and fearful as the one before, nevertheless we will tell you its workings, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then loosen the scrotum supporter down to your thighs, exposing all the vessels that are near the penis, and bind them tightly with straps and extend them; then cut with a sharp spatula in a crosswise manner between the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then flay from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle with double thread, and tie it at the first place where the pus came out, and tie it firmly to the other end; then cut it in the middle straight according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted humors; then treat the wound as the others where you inject broth, so that no vessel breaks that nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels come visible, then it is necessary to drain the testicles from all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the bone 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or goes to the bone, or the stretching on the belly in the part of the intestines, for which the intestines descend from that fracture to one of the sides; and this fracture is either of the bone or of the stretching of it, and these two manners come from much of the causes: either from percussion, or from a jump, or from a fight, or from lifting a heavy weight, and by similar things; and the signs when it is from the stretching of the bone are that it happens little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal right up to the buttock, because the bone presses on the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the bone, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscesses diverse appearing, under the skin nearby, and it is for the exit of the intestines and the body outside the bone. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never detach the intestines with the nerves, and they are held therein, and cause great pain to the patient, even when pressed. 
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron instruments, it is fitting to avoid them because of fear. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;
