et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is such that you command the patient to hold the intestines in his hand inside the wound, if he can reinsert them; then let it be sewn up at its neck between your hands, and loosen the thighs; then raise the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles from their length; then insert within the lips of the scrotum one-inch needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the bones may be able to emerge; then flay the fatty layer that is below the skin of the testicles until the white fatty layer hard is uncovered on all sides; then insert your index finger into that which lies beneath the testicle, into that which is between the white fatty layer that is below the skin of the egg, and the second fatty layer, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second fatty layer; and afterwards push with your right hand into the heart of the testicles, and raise the white fatty layer upwards towards your left hand, and loosen the egg from all the fatty layer towards the scrotum; and command the attendant to extend the egg upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligature; and with your fingers feel if there is any intestine involved or white fatty layer hard, and if you find anything, put it in the belly below; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the rear part of the fatty layer, that is after the skin of the testicles; after the scrotum, then cut the ends which appear from the thread, until there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the fatty layer, of which we have spoken which is below the skin of the testicles, with a strong tie of two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads, and tie them in two parts so that none of the vessels that nourish it can enter into it, so that an abscess does not come; and put the tie according to the first tie long two fingers from it, and after these two ties leave the fatty layer which is below the heart of the testicles the size of a finger; and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is below the skin of the testicles, until the sinews are severed, and the bow, as we have said before; then apply wool moistened with oil, and put it on the wounds, and apply the tie which we have spoken of. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white sinews as we have said, after the incision, for fear of halting blood flow. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature as long as it bleeds through it; and if it delays in stopping, so be it cauterized with hot water, and apply what we have said, until it bleeds; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.  
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to make the cure with iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as the branch which is together with the viscera, in part way that you tie the vessels, after the cut above lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of he who works, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the angles, as we have said, and opens the veins; and no intestine should come out of the joints, and if any do come out, it is bad, and repair it every hour; and even if it stays too long in this place, the wound or the syphac grows until the intestines come out; and this happens because of the extension of the syphac which is in the angles as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swells the veins and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and that is the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture swollen in width according to the quantity of three fingers; and then pull out the syphac which is under the skin than usual, then take a hot iron and put it on the exposed place of the syphac; and press it hard against the belly, then sew the two exposed veins of the syphac onto the head of the iron, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the iron, and do not cut the syphac nor stretch the vein or anything else, as I have taught you in the cure of the ramming of intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if the patient washes and cleanses the wound, until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The cautery is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauteries are milder in this place, and closer to safety. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the cords that are inside are softened, and it is made to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin above the natural skin; then brings together the two lips at a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three sutures or four firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure it as other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread. 
dou chastrement	through punishment 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that punishment is begun in our law, and for this it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only in two ways: one is so that the patient may answer truly when asked and truly know the cure; and the other, because we often need to punish some animals to help us, such as a goat and a sheep and a cat and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that punishment is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and hanging; then take them in your hand until they are replaced and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the castration by cutting: you must hold the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut above each testicle with one cut, when you have well scraped them; and leave no mark on the surface or the fine surface that is over the vessels; and this manner of castration is milder than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction some part of the testicles may remain by chance, so the animal desires lust; then heal the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is according to two manners like men: one so that between the two testicles appears also as the shape of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes even urinates. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has upon the loin also like a penis and two testicles. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure for the man and the woman is that you cut away the added flesh, and cure it like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine passes through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.  
de la tentigene	Of the tentering 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenting is added flesh upon the natural part, so long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the superfluity of the tentigene in your hand or on your fingers, and apply it lightly; and do not press too hard, lest blood flow from it, then cure with another cure until it is healed; and to a char that is born at the mouth of the wound, and the emplast, and perchance jumps out, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and therefore the ancients called it "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you apply it, as we have said of the tentigene, and cure it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of erratics 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pores are small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that has come; or it is by added char, or through subtle or thin substance, and it is made hard in the womb, or on the side, or below, or wherever it may be; and it hinders conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers; and the knowledge of this is by looking at the belly.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the splinters are close together and appear on your two arms or right.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of a subtle kind and is close to the two lips, hurry yourself and do this: put your two index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back, spread her legs; then stretch the two lips as far apart as possible until the subtle splinter is gone and the splinters are out; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman rest at home each day so that she cannot sew. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the splinter is hard and thick, you must cut it out with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the splinter is from a chariot wheel, suspend it at the elbow and cut it out; and have medicines that staunch blood, such as alum, dragon's blood, frankincense, mixed with plenty of egg yolk; then apply a broad splint of linen so that the wound cannot close; and let it remain for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then it should be cured with other remedies until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a sore comes to the breastbone, if it is necessary to cover according to this manner, unless they are festered boils. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For a festering boil that is on the breastbone, one should not touch it with fire.  
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without a court are accustomed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become swollen; and we have said in the division the resemblances of others, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.  
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and swelling, when they are well established in the breastbone, and they do not appear to the touch, unless it is cured by iron.  
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the breastbone, which one can feel, are those that one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then take the uterus with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicines that restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster from it on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if you make her have cupping on her back and breasts without cutting; then take wool, and moisten it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply it to the place. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has subsided, treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh chief, so you must cover it as I have said for the thulul; and then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the cheek
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the cheek, such as chancre and putrid abscess and herpes and esthiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore it is fitting that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the cheek, which is not among the abscesses that boil up; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see whether the abscess is angry at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so you can see it.  
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let it rest until the pain is relieved; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he can lean, and support himself on his back and assemble his feet towards the parts beyond the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then turn him towards his right side, and he prepares the instrument with which one operates the mouth of the wound, from which the form will come afterwards; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being prepared, you insert the tip first to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary for him to put the nozzle of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened, and you press it gently with your hand, if it is necessary to cover the head, apply a bandage at the end; and when the bowels are emptied, you must put softened tents in oil of roses or green oil into the wound; and place the tent firmly from the edge of the wound to the furthest point of the margin, and then apply above the margin and the surrounding area clean linen moistened with water in which rue or mallows have been cooked. Then treat it afterwards for two days with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the margin and the wound by an enema of water and honey, and then of water with long-cooked lily roots and aristoloche; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed at the margin, you must be careful not to cauterize it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the nature of childbirth, and its signs, which are when you see a woman hasten down, and desire to smell the air: then the infant will hasten out. Then you should know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the delivery occurs under her head, with the secondine following; and when you see these signs, it is appropriate to press lightly on her belly so that the infant comes forth quickly. For when he descends head first, the placenta follows, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleansing. And this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes forth on its feet, and the body or the shoulders and hands come first, or it comes forth on its belly, or often, and is turned by chance beyond its neck, and by other bad positions; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures and how one must help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon her head by natural issue, and the woman delivers with difficulty, and the strength of her is weak, then have her sit on a saddle where women hold her; and let oil or fenugreek be cooked and then pour the potion between her thighs with the small spatula whose form is this: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and press at her fingernail until the moisture that is within runs out; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends; and if it does not descend then it is necessary to give the woman an enema of fenugreek mush with sesame oil; then have her drink and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be delivered. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out first, then it is necessary that you gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a stool and lift her feet up high; then tip the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when tipped; and if the hands still cannot enter and the child is dead, then cut the hands with the knife that is placed before this, and extract the child and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the delivery of the child upon its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, if it is crooked, then straighten it upwards and then turn it little by little until it is straight then take it by the feet and stretch it little by little. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to its thighs, if commanded to grasp and make it sneeze from a condition; if it jumps further may God will. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as straight as we have said, then turn it little by little until it conforms to the natural shape. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be lighter. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as far as we have said, then take muscilage of ivy, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and put it on the nature of the woman within and apply this ointment, then let her sit in lukewarm water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make her a collar of myrrh, and place it below, and leave it for an hour; then let her sit upon a seat, then let her sneeze and pull out her mouth and nose, and gently take hold of her belly, for the child now jumps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child upon its knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it puts its arms on its breast little by little; then let it be swaddled upon its neck, and let its feet hang down, and let it lie upon its belly; and fold its arms little by little, and then take its hands upon its belly, and remove the cushions from beneath it, as long as it is shown downwards; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them upwards, then move its belly upwards, then push its hands; and lift the child little by little; and command the woman that she hold on as long as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes forth with one hand hanging down  
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, let the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, let her sit upon the bed and untie her legs upwards; then administer the muscilage that I have spoken of; and if she does not give birth, let her sit upon a chair, then study to bring back the hand; and lift the child according to its natural form, and let her sneeze, and command her to hold on as long as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the delivery of the child upon its neck, and it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is fitting that the midwife holds its hand, then turns it little by little, and lifts it gently; and when it is equalized, she puts on a natural muscle-soothing mixture of elder and oil, as we have said, then commands her to move a little at a time; and when you have done this, you make her sit on a seat, and command her to hold on; and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the afterbirth  
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes strongly in this manner for all the afterbirth, grasp the afterbirth with your fingernail, as long as the moisture is drained; and if the infant can press on its face and on its neck, grasp it from the shoulder so that it is not held back and the infant dies; then push the infant inside, as long as you have put it in as it should be, and command the woman to hold on at all times: then gently extract. 
de l’issue des gemelz	From the issue of twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are a strange thing, and do not live if born; I know this, that they should be multiplied, and are delivered by the umbilical cord which divides them, and is tied to the belly; and sometimes they issue naturally as one below another, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue awkwardly, the care is as we have said, and let the midwife be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and act so that it is worth saving them. 
de plusors enfans	of several children  
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or several up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is fitting that the midwife knows all this, for by chance such things happen; so do according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and there is no expulsion, and you are forced to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution and has no accident or fear of death; it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her thighs inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister applies two poultices, where she is tied to the bed so that she is not moved during the delivery of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oil with a mixture of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and mixtures; then gently insert them into the womb; then choose the place where they insert the poultices that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is stillborn so that it descends on its head; then put the poultices in her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the groin or near the ribs, and if the delivery is on its feet, place them at the hip and middle ribs; and it is necessary for him to hold the poultice in his right hand, and place the curvature between the two fingers of his left hand, and insert it gently with all his hand, and put the poultice in any of those places that we have mentioned, until he comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the poultice: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then put it against the other forceps, or the third if you need them, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch them equally by moving back and forth to make it come out, and let the forceps have teeth to hold it, as it is in this form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, anoint the ball with some of its oil, and put it in that part, and pull the other part; and if none remains, put this forceps higher up, and do this until all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and he cannot bring it back due to tightness, then it is fitting that you wrap it up in a cloth until it comes out altogether; then put a cup on the jointure of the foot or at the wrist, and thus you should do it with the other hand, and with both feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow at the outlet, or if it has a sharp point, then you should put the pointed spatula between your fingers and press the head and extract the point; or you can cut it with an instrument called "almidach," from which the shape comes along with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and in the same way, do this if the child has a large natural head; then draw the bones together with forceps, and if the head jumps out and is extracted by force, it should be split as long as the moisture which is at the bottom of the outlet comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you should pierce it until the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the straightening at the mouth of the womb is light. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is embedded in the belly or breast, it behooves you to extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and pressing the belly or breast, so that the moisture which is there runs out; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then put your fingertip thoroughly smeared with marrow on it, and draw it up to the mouth of the wound. Then put one or two ounces and draw it further; and if the mouth of the wound is constricted by a hot abscess which has come, you must not work at all, but administer moist and fatty things; and apply plasters, and dressings in hot softening and moistening ones. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the splinter is on its side, and you can put it straight, apply what we have said for a living child; and if there is no power, then draw it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the secondary part. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it brings forth what we have said about abscesses that come in the marrow; and if bleeding comes forth, it should be put in tight restraint, and administer other remedies. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had been dead, then conceived another upon it, and the other was also dead. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to her in the buttock, and swelled so much that it opened, and began with great discharge. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to its treatment, and I thought long, and could not suture the wound.  
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after a few days another. 
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because the womb has no bones at all. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought these were bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound and found bones, as long as the woman was in a better condition; and I left the woman for a long time like that, and it became a small bit of bowel at that place; and I have only recorded this chapter because, when masters find a strange thing, they should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marrow back to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, with which we press the books; and at two turns are the two heads of the two liens. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more delicate than the restrictor and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood I must be two fingers wide, and the edge of the trees I must, and a palm and a half long; and between the two liens there are two adjustments of this same wood which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are fitted into the mouth of the marrow to open when you turn the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, resembling it in subtlety and lightness, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood, according to the shape of tongs; and it shall have two jaws with two adjustments, as you see, a hand's breadth long and two fingers wide; and when you see that the vulva is open with the whole instrument, make the woman sit upon her bed, with her feet dangling and her legs spread, then insert the two adjustments together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand on the whole instrument as you have done with tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vulva, so that the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all assembled and are multiplied in their likenesses; and when the women have them arranged, the work is quicker and higher for men according to their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is inexcusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the placenta is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze intentionally, and remove your hands from her mouth and nose; and if she expels it by this means, well done. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a pot and make a hole or cover in it, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water in a pot over the fire; then put one end of a cane or tube into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and suck until the vapors come inside the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second hand jumps quickly. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not strong, command the woman to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or marshmallow mucilage, and then put it in the nature, and seek the second hand; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straight so that the marrow does not break during extraction; but you must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come and loosen.  
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marrow is narrow and constricted, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, be careful not to pull it out; but it is fitting that he who is at the mouth of the marrow, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then give her an enema with tetrapharmakon ointment; it will carry it away and put it back, and it will come strong; but all the same, when it carries it away a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and weakens the patient.  
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is fitting to use appropriate fumigations for this: none of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman in the retention of flowers and secondine is as follows: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a cane, and the head is inserted into the vulva, and the ends are wide upon the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and until the wick is consumed, and then begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather it is closed by a thin membrane: therefore it is fitting for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and she should keep the child from touching it; then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil upon it, and apply an ointment dressing until it heals. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will remain in place, put or pierce a cane of lead, and leave it for three days, and remove it when the child wants to go to the bedroom. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this dislocation comes from the healing of a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cover that healing. If it is healed, as we have said about the cane of lead. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the fundament are nodules and swellings that come from below the fundament outward, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works and still produces a white or subtle pus and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by those who have them by discharge or windiness when the patient has a bowel movement, and by chance some pass.  
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and to half of the penis; and they reach the junction of the thigh and up to the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula that extends to the base, and does not extend:  and it is that you put your second finger or thumb into the base, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a tent of fine linen or a horsehair until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out through the hole in the form of discharge, flatulence, or worms as we have said: know that it does not perforate; if you hurry to clean it. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the urethra, the urine escapes and cannot be stopped by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, then the sinew comes to the place; if there is no crookedness and the invention of pain surrounds, then it must be left alone, and neither medicine nor ointment will do any good; and in these fistulas passing through, there is no stronger cure than labor, and vanity of foolish remedies that intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not pierced through and is not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his thighs, and put his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a sinew of linen, or of lead if there is crookedness, until you know where the sinew comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, then you must put your index finger there, and if you then feel that the sinew has pierced it; and whether it is uncovered where you feel between your finger the synovial membrane or flesh, then know that it is pierced through; if it does not work at all, then it cannot be healed.  
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We say that one can indeed heal some, but this rarely happens; and the help we do is if we heat a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula as it was previously said; and we put the whole thing hot into the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and we do this two or three times until you know that these foul humors are purged, which resemble a bird's feather; and then we heal with tents softened in butter until these humors cease, and then we heal with anointing ointment. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters but does not reach the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of pus or phlegm, and you see the fistula through this which covers the heart; if you cut from the beginning of the fistula and put it forward before the tent, then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be released and will fall out; then cleanse those foul humors that resemble a bird's feather so that none remain. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood comes, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For cautery with fire brings two good things: namely, the burning away of those added humors, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat wounds softened in butter or crushed herbs, as long as the pus flows out, and if the flesh is burned within the wound; then treat the wound with ointments made from dried herbs that harden. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return. 
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the bottom of the fundament and is far from the body, put it back in with your finger or a stick, and inquire about this. 
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between them is a cloth or a seam or flesh where it is about to burst, there is no other way except for trust and hope through the administration of one of three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to its base, or if it can be done put in tents and treat as first; and do not go too deep towards the fundament lest you cut the ligament that holds the fundament, and involuntary evacuations come through that opening. Then treat it as we have said; it may be healed, or remove that covering and clean it once it has been cut away from the fundament, either by tent or other pointed instrument; then cleanse that corrupt flesh in the wound as much as you can; then try to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the part beyond the fundament: this will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is either near or at the foundation of the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you put the twisted thread in it, and put the tent on all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation within, then pull out the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger or the foundation; and grasp the head of the thread, and join the two sides together, and pull one from the other, and leave it for one or two days; and restrain it sometimes, until the threads hold those pieces which are between them, and they close up; then heal the wound until it is closed and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in every way that you can, if it is not too swollen up. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make a bandage so tight for healing, and then cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spathe used to make a fistula is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, for it should not be made as it should not be made, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: either they are inside the fundament, just like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed, and there is one or several, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still bleed a little bit of a sharp citron color or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament is that you order the patient to strain to go to the bathroom, as long as the fundament allows him to see the threads; if it hastens, and can be grasped with tweezers, or you hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the lancet cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them, and powder some hot powders on them that are in place of a cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot prolapse, give the patient an enema with a mordant and sharp clysma to wash what is in the fundament so that it can prolapse openly; when the patient strains, and if the threads are outside of the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, then draw the thread over and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it be wide; pull out the formed thread and tie a knot on it, and remove the needle, and do this to all the others, and leave one for correcting the excess blood; then put upon the foundation a softened cloth in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he should rest; and then leave it until they fall off, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointment and other care, until they are healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	on the drying of the veins or foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying of the veins in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no avail. 
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you remove the skin at the point of a spatula or with your nail, which will not let it get wet; then you treat it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, you begin the shaving again more strongly than before, until it heals well and is skinned; then you treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	Where there is trembling 
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small false appearance against the flesh, and it goes very far in passing; and sometimes you find cold, and one feels it also like death from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more on the hands than elsewhere. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a cane from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that cane on the trembling, so that the circles completely enclose the trembling; then turn your hand around the whole cane until you touch everything all around the trembling, and put it in passing, and extract the trembling from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make one of a chain of iron or steel according to this form, and it shall be subtle underneath and strained above: 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, for it must hold onto the pain, and it must be pressed. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or artichoke, or of melted lead or malleable iron; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and pained, are small.  
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema, both small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:  
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it has a separation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head is pierced within; and it has on one side two holes, and on the other one; and the belly or where one puts the medicines is made of a bladder of an animal or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and there is one finger's space between each hole, then put into these holes one strong thread of raw hemp twisted in X or round about, and assemble the belly as it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and this is the shape of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister holds it in his two hands together until it is all gone, then he removes the clyster, and lets the patient raise his legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night, so much the better. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him for a disease of loosening of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then begin again until he is healed. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or abscesses, then let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is removed: 
des plaies	of wounds 
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or wounds where they are made, and of what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, and by the cut of a sword and knife, or a spear or gun or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head that are simple, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.
