Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never with this vein just one rain, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg, and there comes much blood, and from which it jumps out rains; treat it then as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between leather and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "beef disease," because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well from limb to limb as long as it is going through the skin where it travels, and jumps far; and it comes from the corruption of certain humors, as come worms and serpents and lampreys and ascarides or belly worms; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cleaned and milked, if one cannot pull it out except when it goes; then it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong tight ligature, then cut on top and milk it hard, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, remove the eyebrow underneath it, then cut on top and milk it hard; and it is necessary to use medicines for cleaning and dissolving medicines for bad putrid humors, and beware of foods causing putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then can move from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as a worm on her shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and stuck in her shoulder, and then shortly after ran through her whole body, until it reached her other arm; then she told me that it was now turning around her body, just as I saw. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had felt pain move from place to another, but I had not seen it as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, and therefore this constrained windiness appeared; and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are plump, and have moist bodies and full veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this illness being treated, and the patient feels that pain as we have said, if it appears to you so as we have said, bind it above and below quickly, and then cauterize it until that windiness is constrained in its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, let the treatment of those who expel windiness be done, such as fetid pills, and serpentaria pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kind is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and fletched ones; and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces; and those which lodge in any limb lodge according to two manners: either in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.  
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the arrowhead is found in any part of the limb and signs of death, which I will tell you later appear: then it behooves that you refrain from extracting this arrow because death comes afterward in many ways; and when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not perfectly embedded, so treat it and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrowhead is lodged and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is above the brain, is when there are dark spots in vision and stupor and shivering and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it occurs without fever from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and there leaps from the wound white moisture resembling a poultice, and there leaps also like burning charcoal; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment and treat the arrow if it is not embedded. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a stroke when it falls on the heart is that it is near the left breast and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the stroke moves like a pulse, and there comes forth black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: then know without doubt that death approaches.  
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a stroke that never loosens the port is that without spitting foam it oozes from the wound and the throat swells and the patient changes color and sighs loudly and desires cold air.  
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the stroke falls on the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and there comes great anguish and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the stroke falls on the stomach, by chance it oozes from the wound some undigested food.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the belly or gut and does not pass through the intestines, there is no hope of a cure, nor of extracting the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder and the urine both flows and stops, and the patient feels intense pain; know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and thigh and legs and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.  
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you so that you may do otherwise. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow fell or stuck at the root of his nose; I tried it and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any harm. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out with tongs an arrow that fell into the fat of the oil under the paper below, and the arrow was stuck, and one could only reach its point towards the fire, and it was an arrow as large as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the wound was healed, and no bad consequences came to him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears; I shaved the beard, and I worked delicately until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew out an arrow from a man, which had fallen into his belly, and I thought he would die; and then after he had passed thirty days, it did not change its position; I cut above the arrow, and I hooked it, and drew it out forcefully, and he did not have any bad consequences.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow fall on him or his back, and the wound was sutured over; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural position, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural functions. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you see another man who has an arrow fall on his face, and the wound was sutured; and it remained thus causing great pain; and many other similar cases. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I extracted an arrow from a nobleman of the king, which had fallen between his nose and been slanting towards the right side; and the arrow was all embedded. I was called to treat him after it had fallen for three days.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried it with all my subtlety and did not feel it; and he felt numbness and pain below his right ear.  
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for three days and sutured the wound back together, and kept the patient that way for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his flesh, and then he told me. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for three days, until it opened, and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow pushing back at its place; then I continued to apply that corrosive medicine in the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it healed well within four months, and then I enlarged the wound so much that I could put tongs into it, and move it from one side to the other, but it couldn't come out; then I did not stop refining and devising various ways of instruments until one day I took it with tongs well made, according to its form which will come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it and restored the wound.  
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the master judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was entirely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters compare upon very few things, and upon those that are present and lacking, they find nine works and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign things which occur in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs where they are fixed except according to two manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that exits further by the place where it enters is an arrow entered into their flesh, and it does not exit now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it rots and the opening becomes wide; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce around it with a very fine tool, until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not treat it at all, but leave it until it becomes equal after several days, for if the arrow reaches as far as the syfac, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach as far as the syfac, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then engage in treating it. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is much stuck like this and cannot come out by force, then administer poultices around it, as I told you; then heal the place until it is healthy. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a place in the body where it cannot be seen, probe for it with the whole length of your finger; and if you feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein nearby, enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are ears by which it holds on, cut away the flesh in which they are stuck in two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow so that you can pull it out more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until its ligaments are softened, and then treat it, for the extraction will be easier. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, do what we have said about treating it in its chapter; and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and try to draw out the arrow as best you can, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow has come from another direction, or if it appears at some point where the skin is swollen so that you can see or feel it distinctly: then cut above it as much as the tongs can grasp, and then extract it; if it jumps now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it alone for now and then begin the extraction again until it comes out completely; and if it were an arrow there, push it in all the way through; and if it were a bone, and you see that forceful pushing is needed, use an instrument with a pointed end so that the point of the arrow enters the cavity of the instrument; and then push forcefully. And if the arrow is barbed, push the instrument in with the point entering first, to ease the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is lodged in the flesh or the breast or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close, and you can cover it up, cover it; and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see here the shape: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed end is also like a bird's feather, to push at the point of the arrow, as here is the shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and pulling is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there are XVI on the head: to know: II arteries that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries that are in the II temples appearing; and II veins that are in the II corners of the II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is on the head between the two nostrils; and the II jugulars that are at the neck; and the II veins that are above the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly heals are V in each arm: the one is cephalic, and is on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly," and is above the fosse, and it is the one from which one heals, which appears clearly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg or foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the hip pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous vein is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the bloodletting, as I told you, are that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck to a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two strands hanging from the head: then put your finger on it, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, that is the mark; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well in two, and make blood come out as much as you see; then bind and tie it until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for old migraine, and habitual headache, and accustomed ophthalmia, and for the body of acute tears as well; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and with the thumb below his middle finger, he then presses on the artery; then lifts the heart above the vein at the top with his index finger, and puts the lancet beneath, and lifts the vein upward, and cuts it, as you have done in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then bandage it, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them and their cutting, or the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting of the cephalic for diseases of the face that are old, and for migraines, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears; then they take the instrument which is called a "fosseur," of which this is the form: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press up with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again open it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not fitting that the flames be too strong; and bloodletting should not be done across the bone, for the bone is close, and the flame may break if it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with these things: and the ringing in the ears, and redness, and swelling in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is such that the patient twists his neck with some cord as before, then bleeds, and it should be a bloodletting through which the blood flows for a long time, either one puncture or a long one.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are delicate, they may break; then let the blood flow as much as you need, and then tie it up with cotton and bind it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bloodletting of the vein in the nose is good for fever and a sudden frenzy, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, even when it is old; and the quality of bloodletting is that the patient twists his neck, then pulls down his nose with your left hand and takes a long thin vein and puts it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow; do not go too far in, let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the vein: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of the two jugular veins helps with the constriction of the urethra, and at the beginning of menses, and for many illnesses, and for impetigo, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for tumors; and the quality of the bloodletting is such that the patient squeezes their neck below each one, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein for a long time widely, then draw off the blood temperately, or as much as needed; then do the same thing in the other vein, then loosen the tie, and remove all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	Of bloodletting of the lips.  
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bloodletting of the veins above the lips helps with sore in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and nosebleeds and flux. 
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is to make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and also do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein of the veins that are below the tongue is helped after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for illnesses of the eye, and for illnesses of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeder is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein: therefore bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins through which we commonly bleed are bled in two ways: either by puncturing them with a sharp, wide lancet, or an olive-shaped instrument as thin as a cutting needle, and called "anesil"; and they are large and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the lancet is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:  
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening the raised veins full of thick, visible blood, which contain thick and cloudy blood; and this is the shape of the olive lancet: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and it is for bleeding thin veins, which contain thin, yellow blood.  
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	Bleeding from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, or in the neck, or chest, or belly; and it is fitting for the bleeder that he bleed moderately, and that he be careful of the artery that is underneath. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding comes, then you must cauterize it as I have said, and the flame should not be stabbing but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, then you must remove it and change another; or if you want no part of it, or you heal in its place the vein below the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with a knife flame as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you remove the arm so that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife flame; and be careful not to wound the artery when you see the swollen place, for that is the artery: wipe it then. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upward like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: hasten then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops; which often happens. If the arm is tied up, leave it so, and do not move it; let the patient be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.  
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it flows to you, and the medicine is not present to you, then grasp the artery if it appears, for it is the source of withdrawal; and stop the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of mulberry and cut it, and take one of the halves and tie it on well until the next day; if the blood stops, that is good; if not, if the healer, as we have said, uses powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not hard in many positions because of the small size of the wound, and the strength of the bandage on the arm.  
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps it draw blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it behooves the healer to be wary of the nerve that is underneath, and if he points too sharply with the instrument, and finds the nerve, it swells and the healing is hindered, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must make a cut from the instrument at an angle; and avoid the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, so make it long.  
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic helps it draw blood from the head, and helps as well; and it behooves the healer to make an incision with a flame of olive oil or myrtle, for it is the safest of all the veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is fitting to seek the easiest place, and do not worry if one must try the first time, and begin again; and by chance some swell in the muscles when one tries for the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the healing is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know of healing is that healing is administered only to preserve health and to avoid future diseases; and whether the healing is done in one of the three ways which are: to know, cephalic, gastric, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of spring for young people, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and it should be done on the first day or the third, after two hours or three from the day. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but only when need is of day or night, in all hours and in all times; and it does not suit to bloodlet children until XIV years, nor a woman carrying a fetus before the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one bloodlet the elderly who have passed LX years.  
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse their bowels with a light enema, if they have retained much phlegm, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines harmful superfluities which are damaging to the principal members; and one should not bleed someone who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk, as far as it concerns them, nor those who are suffering from dropsy; and one should avoid bleeding after a colic attack, vomiting, flux of the bowels, and multiplication of childbirth in women, and labor, and staying up late, and fasting, and anyone whose virtue is totally lost, or by something of the weapon or of the body; then thin the humors if they are thick, by foods and drinks and by medicines if you have them; then enter a bath if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the left arm near the third hour as we have said; and keep yourself that day from work, and exertion, and lust, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder be taller than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, blood will not flow; then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the bleeder's lancet with a drop of old oil, then place your left hand finger below the place where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not move and fail when being cut. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as cords in a lute, and some of these are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the bloodletters be advised in these matters. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below that place or above hastily, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen and the patient is afraid, leave them for one or two days, and do not tie the arm: perhaps abscesses will come; do not bathe, then begin the bloodletting again if it pleases him; and if the puncture is small, or the vein is cut subtly and you doubt that as much blood will not flow as you see, put all the flame directly into that puncture itself; and work quickly, so that the veins are swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a poultice of oil upon it, for it draws out the blood from the body, and the oil softens the place where the poultice is; and thus administer the poultice of oil in every vein that you bleed, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing does triacle and balm of eggs, when it is put upon the place; if it is too fine the blood will separate when it is too thick. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess should come, which often happens, even when the vein is not bled very often, or when the opening of the vein is small, hasten and put on the place a sponge moistened in hot water and salt for an hour; and it is fitting that you do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it remains at the place after some days without any blackness or greenness, do not harm it; and if you see, put on something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, cress, or something similar.  
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there occur abscesses and swellings at the vein of the basilary; put then your hand on it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of the hand, that appearance is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then putting on any of the things that we have said, for you might by chance cut into an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a wider incision be made, and the flames are wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled often in small amounts, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by piercing; and this manner of bleeding is safe from running of blood and severing of nerves, and it is worth more than a long or wide incision. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one whose body lacks bloodiness, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, let him be bled three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, he should eat softened bread before the bleeding in thick syrup made with honey, aromatic with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a well-smelling syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the bleeding, after a great deal of blood has been released, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and subtle fragrant syrup, and uses the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.  
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to have his arms emptied and bled again, it is fitting that, when he is weakened by great bleeding, he should be bled little by little, according to the amount of his continuing strength.  
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to open his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, then let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to be bled in another place, it should be done on the second day or the third. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has already been heated, and it brings fever; so you must draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening as much as it will let out a penny; then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds so that death does not come in place of bloodletting, for this often happens when the bleeder is negligent; and it should never be done when you see the arm untied and make the blood come out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard upon it; nor if it is curved, that he extends the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but let him keep it still until he bleeds the second time; or put at the point of the flame, until the blood which is frozen at the vein's opening comes out freely, and place a piece of silk sharpened to a point and press lightly upon it.  
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess is calmed. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein beneath the arm is healthier than the vein in the head because it is composed. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The manner of bloodletting is such that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the wrist is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, and then the bloodletting should be done crosswise, not lengthwise or widewise; and let the opening be large, and let the bloodletting be very close to the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is done more in winter than in summer; and the bloodletting from this vein is safer than all other veins, because there are neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is worth against all diseases of the liver, and this is the way: draw the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein swells, if you see it; and if the vein runs sideways, and if you cut through it altogether, it does not matter; and do not go too deep into the flesh because the nerves are under all naked of flesh, then put the hand again in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out as much blood as is needed, put oil and wax on the vein to solder it quickly, and do this for each vein. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein in the left hand is good for the disease of the spleen, and do all as I have told you about the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The saffron of the sop is worth against all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and legs ancient, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its saffron is such that the patient puts his foot in sharp hot water, and rubs on the vein until it breaks, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many reins; choose therefore a larger rein, or at the ankle, which is worth more. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you choose it on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and the vein should traverse as in cutting; and let the flame be numb. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the hot water, and let the vein empty well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the nerves fail the first time, begin again a second time above by one point, for the skin is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do the same to the saphenous vein of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the ankle strong, and its sinew is worth as much as the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient enters or bathes and tightens above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, draw out the sinew in all the ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is worth more that you cope it, for the skin is below, and it is very full of blood to most men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, draw any vein of it that opens or on the back of the two feet, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and draw out as much blood as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and remove it; she is now healed.  
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping glasses 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or of glass, or of wood; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done without striking is done in two ways: either with all fire, or without fire; and cupping which is done by striking and by extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely on the head; and another on the neck; and two on the sides of the neck; and a cupping glass under the chin; and a cupping glass on each shoulder; and a cupping glass on the buttocks; and cupping glasses along both arms; and cupping glasses on both legs; and cupping glasses on both ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone at all, as one does when drawing blood from a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness to cup, or for habit, we should apply them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between; for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swelling of the tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who faint, and see by night blood and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially in the middle of the month, we order them not to be cupped after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The lancing of the vein aids in relieving headache…which comes to them, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is instead of the lancing of the cephalic vein, and it is not fitting that he who is of cold complexion use it, or who has diarrhea, for this does them great harm; and therefore it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those with head colds. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become stiff, and for this reason it is necessary to put the cupping glass a bit lower because of the fear of stiffness. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is in place of the vein in the head and the basilic vein, and for this it is good for tightening of the breast, and splitting of the channel in the groin, and all that, and repletion; and it must be applied a little while, because if it holds too firmly, it causes stiffness or stomach and heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia and migraine, and strangling, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the basilic vein; and you must instruct the patient to press their hand down while applying it so they do not hit an artery, and blood does not flow. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventosations below the chin are good for mouth disease and gum decay and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is placed on the two lips.  
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventosations on the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Ventosations on the elbows are as good as three veins in the arms, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to make too strong a draught, for the flesh is naked of fat and lies under nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	A cupping glass placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids in the fundament and diseases below, and it is fitting that the cupping glass be large and made of horn so that it can draw well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break, and it would make large wounds.  
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the joints, and bladder, and soften tumors; and are placed at the two shins, and the two ankles, but always they weaken the body after long use, and bring emaciation in many conditions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the cupping glass is that you first put it empty and suck temperately, and put it on quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do this until you see the place red and swollen, and see the redness of the blood; then remove it and put on new cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of bodies, for there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores: therefore it is proper to wound once only, and make wide wounds, and deep punctures; and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is fitting to cut twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is fitting to cut a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we only make one incision. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we begin often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce deeply, and the ends should be such that the heart is pierced only slightly, and it is fitting for him who has thick and hard skin, and who has few pores, that you moisten the place with oil that is stimulating and dissolving: if it is in summer, with violet oil or sweet almond oil or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil or lily oil or chamomile oil or other similar oils.  
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluous matter is thick and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balm, or oil of anise, and similar things. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person whom one is treating has tender flesh and large pores, it does not suit to put any oil on, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or water of mullein, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.  
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture should get up from water of rosemary, or of sumac, and similar things.  
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.
