And those who have large superfluous humors should get up from old wine, or water of vinegar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it does not suit at all to apply cupping before a bath or in a bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping, and it suits him to wash himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped.  
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one who is healing is choleric, and if his wound is too inflamed; it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at leisure, and similar things; and eats little, and meat of a young boar, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine halfway between old and new, and eat little, and eat young pigs and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he will have himself cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes triacle or musk before or after the cupping, to comfort the principal members; and let the wound be subtle, but it is not right for those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Cups that are placed without wounding are those that are placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and gout, and on the belly and buttocks and loins and hip, for these members do not suffer to be wounded on them, and we only do it to draw blood from member to member, such as we place on the breasts when a newborn is healing; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as we place cups on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the member; and to remove pain, when there is opilation or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the opilation, or detaches the stone from its place; and thus it does when it is placed on the liver and on the thigh when there is retained windiness, and these cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot water, such as in diseases of pleurisy, and in this way one fills the cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for it have been cooked.  
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is this: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It has two fingers in width and half a palm in length, and it has on its side near the middle a small hole, like for inserting a needle, and it is made of brass or horn so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb; and it has in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron to put an ignited candle into, and they come in large and small sizes according to the illnesses and the age of those who use them; for cupping glasses for children are different from those for the elderly, and those for thin people are different from those for fat people. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must apply this cupping glass to the limb in this way: take the candle from wax or linen thread and place it within the cupping glass through the crossbar that is in the cupping glass, such that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and your two thumbs should be on the hole that we have described, so that when you want to see if vapor is rising, you can remove the cupping glass; and take the linen thread as before, and begin again often, if you need to. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered for pleurisy, in every acute case, it has neither stalk nor hole, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is put on the limb only; and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are administered only in limbs where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in those places without flesh, such as bone or veins, and other similar ones; and the quality of the user is that when you find cupping glasses that are in soft water, clean without pores, take them. Put them for a night in soft water, until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies; then let it be bled from vein and cupping glass, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the cupping glasses; and when they will be full and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, put it, because it is worth much afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, if you raise it with ease, and then sharply, very well, and then splint it; and if the veins are too close to the body, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it until the vein is numbed; and if there are multiple veins, apply ground vitriol, or galena, and similar things, until it is numbed; or you can apply half of peeled beans to the area, and leave them until they burn at the site, so that it will now stop; and if you need more, take other veins. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the area with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the vein issues, and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they are falling out, sprinkle a pinch of ground aloe and salt, or ash, so they will now fall off. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the people who read this chapter will never have seen anything like it in any ancient book, nor will they have read a letter of it; and for this reason the science is foreign to our land, because I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it except through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in the two previous chapters. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting then that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and dwells on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or strain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to heal the sick person on one side and the other, if nothing hinders him, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his time is not very good, or too cold; and forbid cold meats, that is to say cold joints, and meat from birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb; if the sick person returns to his first original government that he used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that promote swelling, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and peas, and veal feet, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with some swelling the muscles are recovered more quickly and the fracture heals faster.  
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well rejoined or soldered according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, set the broken bone with strong bandages which bind and join the limb together, until it is strengthened as it was before; and do not move it at all from its place, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with substantial foods, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the skull is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to splintering, and another in sharpening, like the point of a pen for writing. 
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with a tiny crack altogether.  
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own treatment and instrument for restoration, according to what memory comes back into place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted and clearly appears so, and it sounds upon pressing with the hand; and when there is neither twisting nor sound upon touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting or a crack or a small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that come afterward, and then extract it now subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that for a fracture that goes in splints, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary now to put them back together equally, just as abscesses that come hot; and if hot abscesses come, leave them for a day, until the abscesses are appeased; then put them together gently and wisely, as you can lightly and wisely; and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then extract it, as it is fitting afterward. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are two broken pieces, whether it is hand or foot, or at your hand it is small limbs, or two strings, or one string and at your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape so that when the parts of the broken limb are freed, then gently join all additions in their places as you can, and take care that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right; if it sets beautifully, and do not force it too much, nor press as those who by their work bring about a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, chastise the patient well so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and be sure that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not quite right, and it must be put in a different position so that he feels no pain; and make sure that it is set straight, so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and shape. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and the like; it is fitting to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs; it is fitting to wrap them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it equally on all sides, so that there is no blemish. Then tie around splints lightly, three turns or four according to the limb, and restrain your hand a little at all the bandage, then go above the break and restrain it less, so that the break then moves a little away from the break; and soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large portion of the healthy place, then take up the other bandage, and turn around again directly on the broken place. Then return to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, not too tight nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above. Then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloths, until they are all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing to the hot abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days; then strain on your splints, and they should be half the width of a cane, or wood from which one makes wedges, or palm leaves, and they should be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it suits the limb, whether small or large; then strain on the splints as you did at the first time, then tie a thread evenly over it, as in the first time on the fracture; tighter underneath, looser above; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen some foolish people who make their bindings with twisted linen cord, it is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not right that there should be less than two fingers' space between each splint. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore from the heads of the bones after the tightening in their healthy state, then put under them poultices of flax, or shredded wool, so that they do not blanch. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.  
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all the broken limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to put splints any firmer than after 5 days or 7, or more according to your surety of a hot abscess arising; and see here the manner of the ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and it is that you take flour that stays at the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg white, and put this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster that restores a fracture in many positions, and even for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster to restore fractures and dislocations and torsion: take three abareis and ladani and enule and asefetide and gum arabic and mugat, each ten grains; myrrh and aloes, each five grains; alechil nine grains; and make a powder, and mix them with the white of an egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly and is worth more to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for torsion: take mugat and vismalve, each ten grains; myrrh and aloes, each nine grains; acaice six grains; bolic armenic ten grains, and grind well, and confect with vinegar or the white of an egg, and administer it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothes the pain arising and cuts down the size of the bone and the fracture: take new wool and moisten it in lye and cooked oil, and put on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removes the pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of common poppy, and grind together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to soften what remains of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take mallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make a stronger plaster than the first, when a hard abscess comes for the restoration of the limb.  
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take mallow roots, flax seeds, betony, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one should put on a broken limb, to restore it, dry things a bit warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair chopped up, or bird feathers, and vervain, and mix them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and bind it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then untie it a little while after, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor that the bone moves from its place; if not, do not untie it for several days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or rest or swelling, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool soaked in water or rose oil on it, and tie it up for a night, as long as you are sure of a warm abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then start the tying again subtly, and a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before; and be subtle until it is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess grows and reddens and pains and swells, I have removed it altogether, and you need plaster and binding, if it starts again as you did first equally. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, then do not untie it except after three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the fracture heals, and the joint approaches the flesh above; then restrain it more than at first, and thicken its flesh as I have said before; and if you see the place dry more than necessary, know that healing cannot come; therefore apply a warm compress every time you untie it, even every third day, and open a small wound there. By this work, you will therefore stop the pain in the limb and quickly remedy what fools do who leave the limb twisted: this is bad, and these are dangerous works, and I see nothing else to do but to leave it alone and work on it straight.  
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various manners of fracture 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many manners of fractures and various shapes, and the causes are predetermined; for there are fractures that are made by percussion of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone up to the sinew which is beneath the bone, as a hatchet or axe does; and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "hachure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt impact, or a fissure, or a neck from a stone, or a fall onto a stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is upon the bone, and this wound is either large or small.  
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is rejoined to the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the piece of bone go down, and the edges are chewed up like the cauldronsmiths when they fire up on the kettles; so the stone goes inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or have wet bones, such as the head of a child; and it happens to all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are detached like tiles; and I will speak about them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquiry into the attempts, and by the rotten flesh that is upon them. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	Hairlike resemblance is known by this: when one has exposed the bone, and rubs gently upon it, if a black break appears. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the patient’s symptoms, and if you see any bad symptom, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, trembling, fever ague, and if the boils come out strong and red, and other similar things in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a worrisome symptom, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment. 
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the time that you can. 
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone becomes corrupted and accidents come which we have mentioned. 
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the divided part thus: and that you take the head of the patient carefully, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and above the figure of the wound more often than you can, and if discharge of blood comes to uncovering the bone, or abscess forms, help him with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscesses are appeased, and you are assured of the discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is if you cut at a narrow section in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another incision larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of different sized incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of hardened iron; and work lightly so that you do not crush the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer incisions with trephines, not too deep so that they do not go beyond the bone into the flesh, and it must have above the point a margin or a circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one comes in its place according to the shape of the bone, so that you have trephines for all flesh; and this is the form of the three manners of trephines. 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put the trephine on the bone and turn it at your will until you know the bone is pierced; then place the trephine elsewhere a little afterward, and thus do all around, then cut with incisions the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as tongs, pliers; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the dura mater. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and made an incision, it is necessary that you leave the instrument which has remained from the bone to all other instruments resembling a chisel, but it is necessary that it be thinner and more subtle than the other chisel; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is that which Gallien says, which is safer; and he praises it very highly, and this is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you place under the head of this lenticular chisel, of which this is the form: 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and it has the part sharpened on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet on top, so that you chip lightly around the bone, and take good care of the cloth which is underneath; if it is torn at the bone, remove the bone lightly, for one can remove it well without harm, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce as far as the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to scrape away that roughness, and remove the scales with a delicate razor which you must have in various quantities, so as to administer the most suitable one in each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with large razors, and then use more delicate ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well done. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle cuts and fractures, it is necessary that you administer according to its direction; and this is not something that can be answered by one who has put his study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sciatic is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the sciatic, then administer another bandage on top, and do not tighten it too hard except so that it holds the wound only; and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and then administer cleansing medicines without biting; and see that the wound is clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to gather, because when pus gathers on the skin of the brain, it will corrupt and spread, and cause the patient great harm; because when one puts something mordant on the sciatic, it irritates above it.  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful, do not doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come except for the medicine that has been put on it, so that its virtue may have effect, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and in glue one cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure it in a manner as is fitting, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both of the bones above are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, only it bends or twists, and then heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should take your little finger or thumb and put it in the fracture, and hold it with your index finger at the pouch, so that the bone returns to its natural shape; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot return to its place, then you must put it equal to the head of a nail a large puncture. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, you do the same, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscesses that have formed are calmed, then bind at the head of the knee bandages of linen, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other from the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the knee. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that one must moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day.  
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary for them to be moistened in a confection of egg yolk and mill flour; then leave the bandage on until the bone is solid and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use goose feathers in place of bandages, and if you wrap it with a soft cloth, hold the fracture there, and blow on the patient among. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come while you are working, put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a drop of diascordium. 
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come, put a plaster on top, made of sesame flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then put it on light compresses, and do not bind the limb at all; and if the fracture in the limb is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with instruments suitable for this, then sew up the incision, and treat it with things promoting healing of flesh, and soldering, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the limb, treat it with tents, and put splints of wood, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jawbone 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is completely dislocated below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly displaced, and not broken in two, but merely pushed in, so it can be recognized lightly. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, then put your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture inwards lightly, and set it with the other hand by pushing outwards, and make it equal.  
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, so that it is equalized. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or breaking, then bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then put cerate on the broken mandible, and place one double cloth over it; and place a large well-made star on the cloth, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it up at the points that you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.  
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, loosen it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; and apply a plaster made from mill powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour after removing the cerate; and put light linen on top of the plaster; and if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not change, leave them until they are healed; it is often healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses should come, treat them as we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, check to see if any part of the bone has been removed; if it is subtle, use suitable instruments for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need. 
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remain none, if the wound bleeds, if it is wide, put on it dressings suitable for that, to promote flesh, until it is healed. 
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times in front, towards the shoulder, and the breakage is according to III manners: either it is broken and detached into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a breakage with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the works are such when the breakage is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps is broken; and the other extends the neck toward the part; then put the breakage equal to your will, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor defect. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to further extend it, put under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity; stretch and loosen the force, and pull out the sphere with your hand so that you set the fracture equally as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the bone out from behind because it comes in deeply, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back and put a medium pillow under the shoulder and push the ministers' shoulder down so that the bone of the arm is raised.  
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then straighten the fracture according to your judgment, and if you find it broken, it is necessary that you split it up; and pull the pieces gently. And if the bone cannot join because of any swelling, then fit it to one of the incisors that you have; but put under the arm this instrument, in order to guard the joint:  
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not notched, and is as wide as it suits it, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you have made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, so cauterize the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, so apply the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, so moisten the cloth in rose oil and alum and wine, and put it on top. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powder from the mill and yolk of egg, and put light swabs on top, and put a spear under the armpit, if you need it; then take a very large bandage of a hand's breadth wide, then put the cloth double on the swabs, and the plaster; then take a thin stick of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage up the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit; and loosen it from each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you see clearly that the stick does not move on the broken bone, so reward it every day, and when the bandages loosen, so restrain them; and make the patient lie on his back, and put under his armpit a small pillow when he sleeps, to lift the shoulder up high; so it will lighten the fracture by the relief of the shoulder, or you tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents come, until 20 days; then start the plaster again, if you see that he needs it, and remove it and leave it like that, as long as it is restored; and it is restored at most in 28 days, and less for some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder is broken or displaced in a wide area and cannot be felt except by touch; if you arrange it according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in all the ways that you can, then put on the spot powder from a mill with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and put a double drape over it. Then put on top a wide and thin splint, a bit wider than the shoulder, and if beneath the splint there is any hair anywhere on the shoulder, use those hairs as bandages of linen so that the splint lies evenly; then bind it all with a large bandage firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and examine the binding every day. And whenever it loosens, untie it, and adjust the splint if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, untie it and be sure, for it is not a bone that is set back easily.  
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes in front, and not below the heart, then lift it up, and the bone-setter, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe a hot abscess. 
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the wrist
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The wrist is sometimes broken in the middle, but this rarely happens; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it descends below, and the patient experiences great pain, and lack of movement, and thirst, and possibly vomits blood, and the hair grows on the broken bone, and he feels well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with his hands, and subtly puts them equal in all the ways that he can, so long as the figure of the bone is as it should be; then he puts plasters and bandages on top of the subtle plaster of salt, or other light herb, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it above the broken bone, so that it does not move; and he turns the tie round to the back, and tightens it carefully, and examines the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, he tightens it; and if it is necessary to untie it because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then he hastens, and unties it, and removes the plaster, and attends to what has come about in a manner of cures; then he reapplies the plaster, and unties it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes behind them, in their thickest part and especially inwards, and they can only break because they are slippery; and one feels it well on questioning by two. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the setting back is such that you put the break in its right place, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a plaster and bind it with a splint, if you need to. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break in the ribs leans inward, the patient feels great pain and shortness of breath, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lining; and they have a sharp pain, and cough up a lot of blood, and this is very dangerous, and the ancients have said so.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is right to give foods that swell the belly, to push back the break.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, that hot abscesses come, unless they have already come. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then we heal it. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that we put cupping glasses on the place to suck out the humors, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not attract superfluities to the place due to weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the place with linen soaked in hot oil and place bandages between the ribs to evenly distribute pressure around, then it is treated with a poultice of pleurisy root, meat, and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot suffer because of the bone pressing on the cloth and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut open above the place of the broken rib, and a tool should be placed underneath to protect the lung; then you must saw through the bone and pull lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound together if it is large, and treat with poultices until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put it on cloths softened in rose oil, and place them upon the area; and treat while the place of it requires for an abscess, and let it lie often on the side where it is, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	Of a broken neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there comes a fracture of the bones in the neck, and so it happens that he falls; and also to the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know whether he will be healed or not, if you take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in several ways, and if he moves them and feels them well when they are pulled out and pricked, know that the joining of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be healed if care is given to him. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healthy or not, see if its feet are softened, and if the accidents are in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without will; and when one turns it over onto its stomach, there is excretion without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned over onto his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in its treatment.  
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, the thing is lighter. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you examine whether there is a hot abscess; if so, put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is appeased; then put a comforting and drying plaster on it, and bind it with a linen cloth, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to operate on the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment smeared charcoal, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is fractured, which is called the “head of the cow,” put your left hand under it, and hold it equal to the other hand in your power, then put on the plaster and the bandage over it, if you need it; then remove it, and if there are broken bones, do the same, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It sometimes happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, there is only a slight weakening at the head; and it makes long, and bends downwards, and the patient has pain in the area, and numbness, and swelling where it is broken. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it, as long as you are above the fracture; and know which is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then place it equal so that it has its natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it slopes inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of this fracture appears to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it equal, apply a plaster, then put a splint of wood or horn on top and immobilize the fracture so that it does not move; and bind the area below the ribs so that the ligature is even. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side, or on their back. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses should come, do not touch them until the abscesses are calmed, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration and immobilize it as is proper if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
