Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, so one must restore it according to one of two ways: one of which is that you take a splint plain of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two cords and lift them up, and place the patient on a seat; then lay the broken arm on the splint, as far as the armpit, and give it a curve with the splint, then put it under some heavy thing or have the assistants hold it down; then adjust the break so that his hands are together, as long as the break returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one puts the patient on his back and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one should hold what is above the break with his hands, and the other should hold below at all the ligaments, and each stretches to his side. 
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their respective parts. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is fitting that you put one ligature halfway below the armpit, and the other towards the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is fitting to place the ligature lightly, without effort, as long as the fracture is aligned on the limb and on the elbow; then align the fracture, as it should be, and extract it, if abscesses do not form. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do form, do not extract it until 7 days have passed, and apply softened linen with rose oil, until the abscesses are calmed; then extract it, and the method of extraction is that you place the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and apply the cloth, and extract on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers' breadth of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingerbreadths on each side; then strain on the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter upon the fracture, tighter but not too far apart. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the splints and the constriction as we have said, in the hour that you bind the broken limb, and you doubt a boil might form, leave it bound until the seventh day as we have said; then look at the binding every three days, so that itching does not occur, nor swelling, nor it comes to the place where necrosis may come to the limb because it is too tight.  
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is done, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident comes, do not unbind it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of equal wool, and look every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are not loosened; if it heals by the power of medicine, and give him the meat as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be large. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be kept in place for forty days altogether; and then one must unbind it and administer baths and medicines for dressings to straighten the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and embedded, it will remain to loosen for I day or II months. 
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of II bones, which are called the two "fosciles", of which one is small, and it is the one that fills the pouch; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; by chance, the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fosciles are broken, the restoration is light, and so is the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are both broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small foscile that is broken, then you must gently extend it a little, and set it equal.  
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone, then one must restrain more strongly; and stretch it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the other toes, and have the patient crossed on himself, and the cushion in front of him higher up, so that the patient does not suffer any strain; then extend the minister's arms below his hand, or at the ligament, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place; and if there is none detached that you can grasp with the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision on the bone, as we have said before. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; so take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration boils should arise, then apply a poultice made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the poultice on top delicately, until the boils are soothed. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote, and apply a plaster made of miller's powder with plenty of egg yolk, then put on the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be now stronger, and one notch wider than the others; and know that it should have six splints or arms in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and pull more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths which are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread with which it is pulled be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the ligament after a few days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you bathe the limb in hot water, until the itching is calmed; and let the limb not be tightly bound at rest. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the strapping again, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones are loosened, and similar things, so address it. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary that you loosen it a bit, and leave it like this for a few days, until the nourishment comes back, and then remove it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not untie it for up to 20 days.  
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Where there is a fracture of the collarbone, then he may put his hands at his neck and have his necks even, and guard against movement and loosening, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and by chance in XX days, according to the humors and complexions.
de la brisure de la main	Of the break of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and as we have two thumbs there are few breaks, and it comes only with much pain many times. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or pained, it behoves that the patient sit cross-legged and sit straight in front of him evenly; then put his hand on a cloth extended, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them evenly with the fingers, as long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and it is wrapped in one linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the back of the calf, make a sphere of rags and instruct the patient to bind it to his fractured calf; then tie it tight with a long rag, and let the star be as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it as needed. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the front, it is necessary that you put a star above and another below on the calf, so that the hands are open and straight, then bind it tight around the hand, and seal the binding between the two.  
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, set it straight as needed and bind it with the palm; and if you see fit, put a small straight star to raise the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, as in the index finger or one of the others, set it straight and bind it with the healthy finger which follows; or bind them all together in a holding position, whichever is best; or put a star on it, as you would on the thumb; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses and treat those who have them, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh  
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is done by tying one ligature above the break and another below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant extends his ligature to his side equally; and this is when the break is between the bones.  
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, one of the ligatures should be towards the hip, and the other ligatures below the break. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then let the ligatures be near the knee, and the extension below; then put the splints on the bone equal with his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and tie it, so that no abscesses come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down then return to your work and your cure; the ligature is made in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a bandage doubled two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and bring the head of the thread above; then turn the bandage on the leg and thigh, then put splints on the fracture, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then apply eight thicknesses of cloth between the leg and thigh to make the tightening even, then begin to tie three or four twists on the fracture; and when you go further above the fracture, make it tighter; then take the two ends of the thread that you put between the thigh and leg, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the head of the thread until you reach the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this until no abscess or swelling or other similar thing comes.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that the bone is broken and set straight as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, then they should be removed if possible; and if not possible, then the place should be cut open and the bone pulled out with force; and the cure should be done as we have said until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And if the thigh is broken so that splints are put on it, as in the shoulder or arm; nevertheless, in this restoration the patient does not suffer. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 10 days or a little less or more depending on the diversity of constitutions.  
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the street of the knee there are few breaks but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, except for a crack or a hole, and it occurs at every wound, even without a wound, this is good. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by putting together what is broken with its parts, as much as it can be assembled; then apply the plaster and put a round star if you need it, and remove it as appropriate, then observe all the procedures that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses and others similar.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and all manner of fracture occurs as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the workings are all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it turns downward.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and bind the splints equally; but nevertheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; and align according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two splints of wood that can bind the leg from one side to the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap it in two cloths above and below, and tie it in the middle too, so that at this binding, the leg cannot decline either to the right or to the left, and thus it is well. And no one should administer any herbs along the length of the leg, and if they are wood, put them on the leg to ward off movement, and properly do this in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or other accident; then cure it as long as it is healthy. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and have to be set, and there are not more forces than assurance in several positions. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a bone in the foot broken, and you see these bones rise upon each other, make the patient place his foot on the ground, as if he were going to walk, then put your foot upon his, where the bones are raised, and press it until they return to their place. Then apply a plaster and bandages over it, and place under the belly of the foot a small board with two inches thick, then straighten the foot gently, after having wrapped it in cloths, and other things which you may need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, then restore them as we have said about the fingers of the hand; then put on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and make it a finger wider, then place under the foot that board which I mentioned, and straighten it gently. And if there are two or three, or more, toes broken, then put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and place the board under the foot; and let it be placed on the head of the board so that it supports the belly of the foot well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is fitting that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each incident accordingly. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone where the knife has pierced  
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman by nature is broken, if you make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the side of her back, and have her held from behind; then fill the vagina with cotton from the nature of the patient, as large as your fist; then raise the woman, and lift the back slowly, and then the cotton will jump out until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and return the bone with the fist.  And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished urinating, put it back in, and do this for seven days or more; the fracture will be restored. And if you see that it is not healing, take a bladder from a young goat, tie a cane to its opening, and insert the whole bladder into the vagina. Then blow into the cane until the bladder inflates inside: it will return the bone to place. Then fill it with cotton and leave it for several days until it heals. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the man's shoulder, or woman's, is broken, if it is restored as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and experience, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates in several ways the right path of restoration; understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's throat and insert it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it and leave it for three days or until healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be healed now so that the healings that we have mentioned testify to this.  
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and there remains some vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour or day, so no abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscess is quieted, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will bring evil accidents. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the heart uncovered, it is necessary that you put it straight lightly with your hands, in a small extension.  
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to put it equal with your hands, then have this instrument which is of iron, which has VII or VIII in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary that he engrave III or IV, according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and have one large hole so it does not bend at compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved head must be placed on top of the exposed bone; and the end at once, so that it returns, and they are made equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, so that the instruments have power. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, then cut with an instrument suitable for this, either an incisor or a saw, according to your ability; then grind away what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you set it back in its place, then moisten the cloth in black balsamic vinegar and properly apply it if it is summer; and do not put any cerate or anything else on the wound where there is oil, for it will cause rot and corruption. Then administer splints when you have restored the bone and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times this has been done by fools, and they have brought death or corrosion upon the patient; and let the binding be looser and softer than for other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then it is not fitting to put splints on it; but wrap around it, instead of splints, hard cloths and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the bandage is causing pain to the wound, remove what you have put on it entirely, and apply a healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in such a way that the bandage runs down lightly.  
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes and it cannot heal but the bandage returns, know that there are small bone fragments, for which you should want the wound with a tent and remove all these loose fragments that cause this pain. 
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place or another way of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it according to what he says in this chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and appears on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not draw it out at all, for many times death comes, but leave it until it rots; by chance it will fall off after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of burns that come from solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the shape of the limb; and by chance, the limb cannot perform its natural functions. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed therefore if it is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together and mix them with astringent wine or with the white of an egg or with oil; and put them on the swelling in compresses, and bind it well and do not untie it for several days; and then unbind it and start another until the swelling is removed; or you can apply a bandage to a piece of lead well made; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it off above, and make the superfluity appear; or you have it shaved by someone until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and the limb remains weak and thin afterward, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages and nourishment could not come to the limb; or because of excessive movements, or too large movements, not at their proper time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.  
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and soften his body, as long as his blood is multiplied within him; and give him baths, and give him joy and rest; then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws great nourishment to it, and warm it often with hot water, as long as nourishment flows to the limb; and returns to its natural shape. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb twisted after healing 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, for many foolish ones have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and it brings great harm, and by chance death; however, if the inflammations and pains are fresh, then it is fitting that they be softened with hot water, or mollifying herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and apply a softening plaster, such as diachylon well made, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with fat of jellyfish or oil of sesame, and make plaster upon it; or take ripe figs, and crush them with bran of flax, and similar medicines that reduce swelling. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And at no time is the dislocation removed by continuous and lengthy rubbing with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuousness is aged and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then you must cut up to the bone with a subtle incisor lightly; and apply caution and study in the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations. 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to anyone, if it is necessary now to bring it back in place.  
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the tissues swell, and by chance if one puts it back in place with pain; therefore it is not fitting to move it when it is swollen: many times this brings spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this occurs, make the patient healthy, then leave him alone until the abscesses are healed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently soften it, and treat each member as the treatment will come in its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws 
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated both, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little loosened from their places, and softened a little; or they are entirely dislocated, and hang down toward the ground, and spill the saliva from the mouth which he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and it envelops his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through several arrangements. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it quickly and do not delay; and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put the tip of one of their thumbs into the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other hands should be free, to apply equal pressure; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.  
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And hold the eye steady until it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it is difficult, even if both jaws are together, then apply a mixture of hot water and oil until they soften slightly; do not pull too hard when returning it, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then put soft cloths soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax on it, and then bind it lightly with soft bandages; and have the patient sleep on their back, with their arms resting between two pillows so that they do not move either to the right or left, nor make any effort to chew, but take light food as long as the pains are gone and the jaws are joined; and then eat what they want lightly, and do not bother to open their mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is well joined and healed. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their places, fever and accustomed soddenness will come, and perhaps loosening of the bowels, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times they died in nine days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from both sides within the continuation of the hip and buttock, and it is dislocated sometimes outwards, and one feels it well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; and then presses the place with the hollow of his hand, and it will return; then puts plaster and bandages on it, and removes it; and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot be dislocated; if it can, and if it dislocates sometimes, then reset it in its place as we have said; then put plaster and bandage on it, remove it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way, the head of the shoulder blade is reset when it is dislocated from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one of which is that it dislocates at the part of the axle below; and the second is at the part of the arm pit; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates below toward the axle, especially in those who have little flesh, for in these it is quickly dislocated; in those who have enough flesh, it is hard to dislocate, and it returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a bruise or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is necessary that you examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a dislocation has occurred when the shoulder is pulled down towards the armpit and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest diversity between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit at the shoulder blade the top of the shoulder, just as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor move it in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, unless it is hidden, for you will find it clearly at the shoulder blade; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to put back in place when it is new, or when the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then puts his thumbs under the armpit, and lifts the joint forcefully upward to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it down below; it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands the next day, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and give him a mollifying and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied; then turn the patient onto their back, and put under the shoulder a wool cloth equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the mire on the patient's heel on the cloth, and raise the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the patient’s hand; and another assistant holds the patient’s head so that it does not move down; this shoulder will return immediately now, and if you see that the resetting is according to this manner: and have a man present who is larger than the patient; and stand straight beside them, and put his shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, and raise the shoulder blade upward, so that the patient hangs in the air. And another assistant pulls the patient’s hand downward toward their belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, they can hold something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return at once. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And resetting can also be done in another way: take a long iron rod and stick it in the ground, so that its head is as round as a pestle, and it is neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, but have them covered with cloths above, and the patient should lie lengthwise along the wood; then extend their hand downwards on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all the things we have said, do this cure: take an iron rod of two arms in length and four inches wide, which has a round head to enter perfectly under the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie cloths under the head of the rod so that the rod does not hurt the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit; and extend their arm along the length of the rod, and tie the shoulder to the rod, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on the rung of a wide ladder, and extend the hand downwards, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return at once. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter the way, it behooves you to put beneath the armpit a sphere of equal wool, then apply plaster mixed with powder from mill flour, incense and yolk of egg upon the entire shoulder and bind it up; then strain it beneath the armpit gently, and turn the ligature over the plaster, embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus. 
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it behooves him to chew a little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then chew more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has been forced out of place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, it behooves you to administer three cauteries to punctures as is set forth in the chapter on cauteries. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is severed or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the buttock and the breasts or behind, if it is done by thrusting and extending of hands, one must administer in another place, and heal as long as he is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness to the limb and tardiness in movement, let the patient bathe many times until that stiffness is relieved and it returns to its first nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder blade is dislocated in points and in points it returns; and if it is dislocated on all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not put back in place, because one sees it well and feels it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you soften it as if abscesses were coming, for if abscesses were to come, it would be a hardship to bring it back; and perhaps it cannot be brought back at all, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than the other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, if it is such that you can bring it back, is that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arms should be spread, and his hands from above according to the knife around, up and down, and push the joint at its ends together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand with his hand, and strikes from the root of the palm or the costal cartilage which is dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and let the one who administers extend the arm, and hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when he reaches the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint gently, until it returns; and when it is in place, put dry plaster with egg yolk on it, and bandage it firmly, and tie the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well aligned, apply the plaster and bandage again, and leave it like this for several days, until it is firmly set; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put a greased sheep's wool on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him go into the bath; and when he sweats, if he rubs the joint moderately, then put the wool back on, and then go into the bath; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see that it returns, put moist, heated cow dung with butter on it, and strain it; it will return to its place. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is easy, lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the tissues are swollen or an abscess comes hot. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is such that you place the sick hand on a table and extend the injured arm, and have them put it straight, so they put their palm on the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns completely. It is necessary to see if it is well in its place; then have the patient put the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient put the back of their hand on the table, and have them put their hand on that appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now returns, it is good. If not, apply soothing poultices for abscesses and leave it like that without starting again. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain twisted; do not harm the patient further than that while his hand is numb and unable to grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut or the artery; there is no other remedy except to burn with a cautery near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it like that. 
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some pain, then moisten with hot water, and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the front; then straighten the finger, and push the dislocation into its pouch until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the side where it is detached; and leave it for 2 days, and then put it straight that day; and at night tie it, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and make it move, and tie it again at night; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the front of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and also do this, when it is dislocated on another side. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	For the loosening of the shoulder blade from the back 
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, if there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the movements jump strong without will, and he cannot hold them, and many times some limbs are softened, either the two thighs or the two arms or one. And many times the shoulder blade moves in four parts; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you consider if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure or healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old ways of cures were spoken in many words, but there is not much profit in all of them; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast beforehand, neither has remedy nor feels it; and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have a strain beneath him, so that he does not become bruised; then put a coal at the head in the earth formed, and the other at the feet, and tie a string under the armpits of the patient, and the other at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two coals; and they are well fastened, the coal as we have said, and the doctor puts his palms on the spine formed, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a table three arm lengths long, and put it under the wall, and let the patient be on his side, and put the head of the table under the wall; then put the middle of the table on the spine; and let the doctor put his feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not, do it to the shoulder which turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you place two burning coals on the head of the patient, one arm's length from each other, and two others near their feet, and between each coal, above and below, a palm's space in length; and have in each coal one hole where the turnbuckle passes, and let the coals be firmly set in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of coals have one turning coal from which the turnbuckles turn, and have in the two turnbuckles two small coals a palm's length long to turn the turnbuckle; then tie the cord which is among the axes to the turnbuckle towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet to the other turnbuckle, and each of the assistants turns his turnbuckle for all the cord, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.
