And when it is straightened, apply a drying plaster with plenty of egg white, then the bandages, and then a splint of a tablet three fingers long to support the place of the gibbosity and the part of the vertebra that is sound, then tie it with a cord as we have said, and use the patient with gentle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, it is fitting to administer softening and soothing medicines with the splint we mentioned before; and sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes on the back vertebra of the spine, and one thinks that it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that appears, for which reason one should not presume: by chance death might come.  
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come out of dislocation alone, not as the other joints do; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more often inside than outside, and rarely dislocated in front and behind. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee at the fire; and there is a swelling nearby that is hot with an abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who it comes outside to, is that this accident is contrary to those in front.  
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has it beforehand are such that his leg is well aligned according to its structure; nevertheless, he does not bend his knee twice without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and his groin swells, and when he walks, he goes on his heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it behind are such that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the level below the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The setting of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider whether the dislocation is old and it remains according to its position, there is no cure, and it is not fitting for him to have any hope. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for one whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four types of dislocation, you hurry to turn the joint, extend it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and does not need any other treatment. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you prepare a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie it on the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he strangles it with a strong bandage on the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and extend upwards and downwards all at once, as long as the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, it is good. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to put care into its resemblance When the dislocation is in the upper thigh, it is necessary that you place the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage on the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the groin, then extend the bandage upwards towards the groin, and towards the calf; then take another minister his arms, and embrace the large part of the sick thigh, and extend it outwards: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong cord above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two fists more than the others; then let it be hung on the top of a pole, and let it be two arm's lengths above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient, who embraces the bottom of the thigh, for the joint will now return quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the back, let the patient lie down as we have said for one who has sciatica, and tighten the cord on the diseased leg properly, and on the foot also; then put two coals, one at the head and the other at the feet, then put one coal between the thighs of the patient in the form of a triangle; and put bandages of wet cloths around so that he does not burn the patient, then let each minister stretch towards him, and the one who looks puts his hand equal to the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table, and press it together as we have said in the treatment of dislocations, and lay the patient on their healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to quickly extend the injured leg, and according to what I have said; and let the patient bear their pain on the injured angle, then press with the other hand, and extend it downward toward the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is backward, it is not necessary to extend the patient downward or lift them off the ground, but rather that they should be as if their hip were dislocated backward, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let them be on their face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and press on the joint at the table; it will be set when the patient extends their legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for three days or four, then untie it and apply a plaster on top; and if you see that they are even, bind them again as before, and leave them for three days; then untie them, and let them walk gently, until their limbs are strengthened.  
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not straighten at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your two thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee; and another minister extends his foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg at his thigh lightly; and put a plaster on it, and let the leg air at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then unbind it; and do not let the patient walk, until the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not present, administer strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel.  
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes moved and sometimes dislocated completely, and inside and out. 
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tight before the part where it is dislocated; the resetting is gentle, and one should extend it gently with their hands when it is only moved. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated altogether, it is fitting that you make the patient sit upright and have them hold their leg firm by the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand and then with your left twice, then extend it upwards and push the foot up nicely; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return this way, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and put a strong beam firmly into the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around them so they do not bruise the patient. Then have one assistant hold the thigh and another assistant extend the foot with their hands or a rope tied around the ankle; then each assistant extends evenly and the beam is now between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when it is extended; then put your hands equal to the dislocation and have another assistant hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.  
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set right, put on a plaster and bandages over it, and bind it tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are on the ankle behind, so that the bindings are not too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and if the bindings loosen, bind them again; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he goes before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, you must soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed. 
des dois	from the two  
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, you must carefully extend them without exertion, and it is a light thing. 
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, you must have the patient sit on a level place or on a table straight up, and put your foot on what appears of the joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is nothing showing, put under the sole of the foot a two-legged stool, then bind it tightly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest as long as it heals.  
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together 
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and you wish to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, do not dare; and use at the beginning things that soothe the hot abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb in its place, so that the hot abscesses may come to life; and when the limb is in place, administer things that soothe the hot abscesses, and treat the wound as it is fitting, with drying lotions; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken off, remove them, and do what we have said in simple ailments; and guard yourself from entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will profit you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.  
Amen	Amen
